O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the essence of medical science, together with its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with you, which is a part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is treated in our region and is strange from all sides, it is very difficult to find the science and knowledge, and it is not delayed by the force of the hands except for the small descriptions in books of the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and the intentions are closed, and knowledge is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or I think that I will make it alive together with the order of this physician according to the path of exposure and explanation and abbreviation; and I will come together with the shapes of the tools of cautery, and the other instruments of the work, with the assistance of the explanation and preparation of it, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who deals with this to surmount in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and the shapes and connections and separations of the nerves, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and their number, and the movement and the veins that move and those that rest, and the place of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, as Hippocrates says, "The non-existent is not with the existent, and with work it is small, and most of all in the art of hands."
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that if anyone is not familiar with the things mentioned above, he may fall into error and harm others; so that I have repeatedly seen many of those who engage in this science and, abandoning their knowledge and experience, are lost.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish man who cut an abscess on the scalp or the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries at the base of the neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another foolish man who was leading a stone-worker's son by the hair; and the boy was very big, so he took a piece of his bladder and killed him in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also seen a man called Lou the Tacker; and I saw the disposition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and if they had tacked him, he would have died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see another case which came for treatment. i. a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the doctor, ignorant, pulled out the break over the wound as he bandaged it tightly, leaving no scar, and left it so. And he ordered that it should not be removed; and it waited so long that the leg completely withered away and the bones came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I had dislocated it, it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the way to corruption was confirmed or member, and he could not make it well; and the corruption did not cease to go through the member until the members were completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another case which came for treatment. i. an abscess which was putrefied, and then inflamed by the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is purred of melancholy humor, there comes no other way than to touch it with iron if it is not in its right place so that one can take away all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into .ij. divisions: namely, where there is danger in many conditions; and I will show in each division of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason, you must keep this secret so that the foolish man cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your weapons in harmony, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that, through the grace of God, you come to salvation and are healed; and ward off your weapons from that which makes you doubt, and believe in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galien warns against some of his advice: "Do not take care of any bad disease unless you are called foolish."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to the following three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are on fire cauters and medical waters, and the final chapter is on the forms of instruments, the tools for cauterizing, and everything necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is on shaping and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the final chapter is on ordering and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torques and similar things; and it is ordered that the loins be stretched up to the chest, and that the forms of the tools be defined.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work, it is necessary that I give the quality of help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest word and subtlest science, and the secret answers to it; and many wise men would speak on this, and agree upon it; and I lack words for these, for they are long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire cautery helps all complexions where there is matter; namely, hot-tempered people who have dry matter and cold-tempered people who have wet matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together with matter, some agreed and said that cautery is great help; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is of no help to disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be cured of hot disease by heat, nor of dryness by dryness; and he who said the opposite, that cautery does great help to hot and dry disease that comes in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man with his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every path, does not interfere but he who has experienced it, and who knows through long practice the cauterizing ointment, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the remedies and the space of time; of other complexions we have no fear, even if they are cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this will come together and agree with the cauterizing.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that a fire cautery all at once so that it is secret and helpful to the cure, and of greater goodness than an aromatic medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes not forward but to the member which is cooked, and does not harm another member as much as it can.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another by moving away, and bring illnesses of great healing to the member, and sometimes they cause sickness.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and because of the goodness of its substance, does not burn, unless there is an excess of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experience and by the length of service and study that I have devoted to the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I apologize for the length of the speech, for it does not please me that I should reveal the secret of fire, which is hidden from men, and the quality of the work, as the philosopher says in his demonstration; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made at the time of the moon's quarter-phases; and let them be said.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all seasons, for because the sudden harm resulting from the aid of cauterization; and most especially, the cauterization is for necessary pains that cannot wait until the season when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And I don't think ever, son, as they do so; for in the illness that is healed by cauterization there is no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they believe, since cauterization is only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine because of its haste in effecting its value, and for its greatness and dignity.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it may happen that the illness comes not according to the complexion of the sick person and his place of illness and its virtue; and are gathered in him the excesses by the acquisition of meat and similar things, if it is not that cauterization is administered in the place where he has a little excess of moisture, so as to do away with pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return; but that happens less.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And yet few people understand that fire cautery is a form of medicine, and this is evident; but they do not believe that cautery is effective after medicine, but their understanding is wrong, and fire cautery is a form of medicine because when we administered methods of cure for various diseases and they did not work, then we administered fire cautery, and it worked.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, understand that fire cautery is a form of medicine, not because of the intentions of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancient ones said that gold cautery tools are more effective than those made of iron, and they stated that the quality and purity of gold makes it superior; they also said that the heat of gold does not cause corruption, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that in some people it does work; and gold cautery is more effective than iron, as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And know that when you heat gold tools, you do not recognize when they are too hot due to the color of gold, and they often cool down soon; and if you heat them too much; then put them in the fire; and so there is enough hesitation.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you shall read this chapter up to the point where the vision is clearer so that you may find it easier to locate.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purified with a solvent medicine, which will remove the pain in 3.3 or according to what the virtue and freshness and the habit of the sick person can bear; and then apply the medicine to the head of the sick person.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then put the cross between your hands, and place his hands on his feet; after that place the roots of your two palms on the roots of his two feet between his .ij. toes; and as soon as you come to him, let him bleed a little, then heat the cautery which is called "oliver", from which this form is:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it over the red mark, and make a small cut as you descend and remove his hand little by little while turning it; then let go of the joint, and rub the joint until you see the bone 1.1 small piece; and if you do not see it, then start the cautery as soon as you see the bone as I told you; after that take 1.1 piece of silk, and put soft cotton in it, and put on the mark, and leave it for 1.3 days; after that put moistened cotton on it; and let it be until it is hot enough to see the bone; then cure the wound with an ointment called "tetrarchal formula", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And say the old one that the longer the wound is open, the more it will be purified; and for this reason if you are in a hurry.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should let the cautery burn so much part of the bone is burned, and then release what is burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said that one should let the cautery burn so much as a woman puts her finger in her cunt to let the humors come out, and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after which one must cure and patch it up.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these 2 methods of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good in all respects except that they might be useful in some men who have a tendency to fear; and I think that I should let them burn, for the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other limbs; and even more so when the joint of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first application of cautery seems to me to be safer and milder, and from this I practice cauterizing in a way that will bring about healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	for the pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Pay attention so that the patient's head is of strong nature and is not too cold; then apply the fire cautery quickly as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying the fire cautery to each horn of the head, as we have said above, and applying the same cauterizing liquid called "vaselz"; then place the vinegar; and arrange your hand so that you do not see the bone: the pain in this cauterization is much greater than in the others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary for the horns to be smaller than those on which we cauterize the scalp, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly in one part of the head there is pain and it extends to the oil, and the head is cleansed with medicinal drugs, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of illnesses, and all this does not benefit: then make cauterizations according to .ij. ways, that is to say, with water medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	When making a water medicine cauterization, take a piece of bark and peel it back and cover it with .i. poc as many times as there are joints, and then apply the temple where the pain is in a partial way that you can dip the bark into the oil; and when it has been dipped, let it lie and tighten well and leave it like this for 10 hours; and then remove it and treat with fresh bark, and leave the wound like this for .iij. days or two days; and then put cotton soaked in butter on it until it is healing well.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil treatment until it is well healed; and if you see that fire medicine may be useful, which I have written about or second healer of burning drugs.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cauterization: Heat the cautery so that it is according to this manner:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Et est apelez "clos" por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d'un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparence; et le met sor le leu doloureux, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l'espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n'arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the form of a cloak or there is little of the collar, and in the middle of a small appearance; and put it on the painful place, and take your hand and turn the fire a little lightly, until the half of the keur espés is burnt; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is distant, and run an abundance of blood.
de emigraine	de emigr
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	Quant tu cures emigraine si com nous avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que le cautere devant dis de la médecine et du fer ne lui soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est appelé "cultellare" tant qu'il soit blans; et signe ainsi sur le lieu douloureux une ligne de demi doigt de long, et osté ta main une fois, et l'estrains que tu ne coper l'artere et que ne viennes jusqu'à l'os; et te garde de la mandibule qui mute quant on mords, et le ner n'ait regart que la mutation et que les spasmes ne viennent maladement, et te garde de la décomposition du sang de l'artere lorsqu'elle est copée, ou copée ait grand peur et surtout à celui qui ne s'en konoit, et qui n'est ni étudiants ni éprouvés; et laisse l'œuvre en mi voie; mais je vous dirai comment on retient le sang lorsqu'l'artere est copée, et je vous montrerai au livre où il afiert en ce traité.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the neck too as we have said, and heal the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization which we have said or the chapster of the extraction of the artery, with the cauterizing knife that has .ij. blades; and this cauterization is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	for pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ears due to cold occurs, and one has applied the solute medicines and other treatments which we have mentioned in the division of this chapter, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cauterization which is called "poins", whose form is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After puncturing all around the ear on the sick side, or around the two sides of the ear where the pain is located, and moving away from the root of the ear a little bit as you have marked the spot; make .x. punctures around each ear; after that, treat the spot until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	which must be cured by cauterization is not strong except for those that move with fluid, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not apply cauterization to similar things which come from dryness and waste of semen.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this kind of torture that moves with fluid from thirst and purging of the head and gargling, and that is not worth it, then you should apply three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, another a little further away in the temple, and the third in the joining of the two lips; and place the cautery in the healthy part, and let it burn for half the time; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the form of the scalpel that we have put forward, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the blade be a little thicker; after cure the place as I have said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, it does no good, and the patient has no fever, so then do 22 cauterizations: 16 on the two horns of the head, and 1 each where it is called "vesselz", just as we have said above, and a cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and be cured just as we have said above.
de litargie	of lime
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	This text describes a treatment for a disease (perhaps cerebral hemorrhage or stroke) involving the use of lime to create a "lime plaster" for the head, followed by the application of a "saffron poultice" made from saffron and water, which is then placed on top of the lime plaster. The treatment is completed with a cauterization process, as described in the previous sentence.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is this way, it is good; and if it is not, then do 22 cauterizations of the scalp by going down to the base of the neck, and space out each cauterization by 1/2 inch; and the cure as we have said before, and if he still has fever, then do 1 cauterization in the middle; and if it is necessary, 2 others on the two horns, and cure him until he is well; and be the cauterizations which are called "olive", as we have said above.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	to warm the head of the patient, then wash it with water and salt as we have said before; then apply fire cautery to the head and to each horn, and behind and above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is strong, apply four fire cauterions to the spine of the back; and let it burn until the hair at the base is singed, and lift your hand; then cure as much as possible so that it is healed, and the cautery that is called "oliver" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	from epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	For those with a feverish reaction to fire cautery, it is necessary to first warm the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the chapter where the patient is very ill and suffering from feverish reactions to fire.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot bear the fire, he makes gargling and chewing to clear the throat with bone meat; after him, he takes the head in the middle, and does 1.i. cautery according to what we have said before, and 1.i. cautery on the neck, and on each horn; and if the patient is far away and suffering, he does cauterizations as I said to that who has paralysis and softening of the spine, on the back bone and the neck, and let the cauterizations be olive according to the manner which I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, he does 1.i. subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, by the cause of melancholy, there are excesses or corrupt humours and thick fluid, then the half-cautery which we have said to that who has paralysis:
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, by the cause of melancholy, there is decline in the excesses towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then he does something to refresh the brain according to what it is before in the division:
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cutting the head of the patient; after making .i. tortois shell out of fine linen, also as .i. circle, put it under the head; and the patient's face should be crossed and held firm from all sides; then present the liniment, and cover it with old sheep's butter; and heat the fire moderately, so that it can be endured by the patient; after filling the shell inside the head, and letting it cool down; and do this to the patient every week once with other good government, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or if you want to cauterize the wound by making several punctures all around it. This way of cauterizing dries up the brain a bit; and then put cotton wetted in butter and in lard on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the signs come first as eyes by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient purifying thing the head, and the guard of all moisture, and let it sweat or bathe several times on an empty stomach.

After he has ordered his head to rise, and made a fire cautery on the head, and made .ij. cauteries on the .ij. temples if he is dislocated from the jaw; or if in the dislocation the jaw comes out of its socket, all the cauterization should be done on the veins and arteries that are behind the cheekbones, and the cautery should be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of the escape of blood, and if you see too much blood come out, then stop it with a cloth as you have.
dou cors des larmes	And two cor des larmes

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Of the tears of fire within the eyes.

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization which is called "Clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cauterization which is called "Olive" is made. Of which this is the form:

dou poil qui point l’oil	The hair that points to the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No one has yet discovered that the hair of the oil is converted to the parched, and grasps the oil, and it is made on 1.1 ways: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then place the patient on your breast; after signing on the paper of the hairs a figure that is also like the furrow of the mirth, and is the beginning of the sign that detaches the hairs; then put cotton wet in pitch and muskellaige of persillion on the oil, and heat up the cautery with which there is this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have signed little by little many times, so that the healing is at the place; and the sign of the work of health is that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs rise to the height of the oil; then lift your hand up, and leave it so for  .iij. days, then put cotton wet in butter as long as the heating is done; after the cure of the wound until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come out, and the paper is softened then restart the cautery on that same middle place, as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper rises to its natural place, and is even, and do not prick the hair oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical hot cautery is that you order to the patient that he leaves the hairs as long as they are even and big, then make of parchment the shape of the furrow of mirth; then take French soap and lively salt, each one a  .Z., and grind them together well; and do it promptly, so that if it does not cool down, then pour on the shape that you have made like the furrow of mirth, and put on the paper of the hairs; and if the illness holds in  .i. oil only, then work also in  .i., and if also in water; and put cotton wet in pitch; and the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	If you have been ill for a long time, keep this medicine at your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the medicine has passed, lift up your chin and hold it up as if it had been lifted by a fire or an incision; and if this is so, that's good. If not, put the medicine back on the spot where the medicine has not worked, until your hairs are long and even, and your nails are cut short; then put cotton soaked in oil over the sore spot called "dysentery" and other spots, until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to hold your chin well up so that it does not move from the medicine applied to your hairs; and if the paper becomes soft after, and the hair is pricked by the oil, then repeat the medicine on the same spot where the paper has become soft properly, just as you have done before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the oil dou mirte:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the hair of men is different in length and thickness, and according to this your constraints; and do not reply the right path to anyone whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not benefit them, then you must apply cauterization according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dip the hair between your hands in a basin of water or wine juice over oil; then heat the cautery until it is red-hot: and apply it to the hair at the base, as if it were a feather; together, let the tip of the cauterium be directed towards the head, so that you do not burn the skin; but rather, let the fire be directed only at the hair.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and treating the porosity, and drying it; and if it is closed, then operate, and seal it with fire; after which, place the hot cauterium firmly on the hair, and keep your hand away from the cauterium at the base of the hair, that your hand does not go wild; and place the cautery in the oil, and corrode it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to cauterize up to the bone, it would be better. If not, then start cauterizing again after one more day, and if you need to do so, and leave it .iiij. days; after that put cotton soaked in water on it until it is healthy, and for ten days after it is healthy, then put medicine with corrosive water until the bone is uncovered; and treat according to what comes out in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And I have a way of cauterizing a fistula that no one of the ancients spoke of. Understand fistula, and cut it; then put in the incision .i. subtle camahan so that this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I form it in quantity of a 1/4 of a pound; and hold your hand where the camahan is firmly, and do not move the patient at all so that the melted plonk does not run to its oil; and it comes if you put cotton soaked in water in a bowl or in a basin: the plonk so art the leu de fistule, and he heals with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good. If not, then it is necessary to pierce the nose, and bring back the fistula to the root of the nose according to what comes out in his chapter.
des crevaices en levres	of the crevices in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	the times when crevices form in the lips, which are called "hair", and most often on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these crevices with the treatment we have described in divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then heat a small surgical scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it firmly in the crevices as long as it comes out clean; after the cure, apply balm to the area until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the palate or the roots of the teeth, after causing pus and swelling and becoming hollow and infected; you treat it as we have said in the division, and it does not help: so you should use a fire cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; then you seal it or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron comes to the bottom of the hole, and behind it; and do this once or twice, after the treatment we have described, as long as he is healthy; and if he is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, you should discover the root and remove the rotten bone according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and the tooth does not respond, then place the head of the patient in your lap; after heating the cautery, shape it so that you can put a wire on the tooth; place the cautery hotly inside the tooth, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the process according to your will; after filling the mouth with salt water, and keeping it there for an hour and rinsing it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And this is the way to treat those who were moving tightly, and the gums softened restrained, and the moisture corrupted dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the teeth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold or sight, and medicine does not help, then there is a need for fire cauterization according to the following two ways: and fire cauterization with butter and fire cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Fire cauterization with butter: Take butter from a vat and stick a small iron or gold wire into it; after that, take cotton and wrap it around the end of a needle, dip it in butter, and place it on the aching tooth carefully; hold it there until the butter cools; do this often until the power comes to the root of the tooth, and if the wool and cotton become wet with butter, and put it on the tooth, and put on 1 iron wire as hot as possible until the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	If the fire cautery is such that you squeeze a ferret-iron or an iron ring, and it's big so that the fire doesn't come to the mouth of the sick person; after warming the cauterizer, from which the form will come later, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer has cooled down; do this often, because the pain will be worse the next day or the day after. And it is convenient that the sick person fill his mouth with good fat in the haste of the cauterizer, and then wipe it off: and this is the form of the cauterizer.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery out of the root of the tooth that you want, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the iron:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of pus and cold dampness, and does not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery tooth with which this comes later, and has 1.3 openings for the fumes to rise from the cauterizer on the other side; and place the cauterizer hot on the abscess once, or if it is small, place the cauterizer according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in that condition for 1.3 days; and put cotton wet with oil on it until the burning is over; then cure the wound with garlic and tar as long as it is healthy.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moisture prevails over the chin, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be voided first by restorative medicines; after which make cauterization at the root of the throat, and guard against coming any further than the throat, and dare not kiss but a little. After making .i. another cautery to the jointure of the neck with the head of the spine, and let the cauteries be called 'clavicle' from which we have the form before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and disease of the mouth are cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or scorbutic illness, and is an ancient disease, then one should make iij. cauteries on the forceps in his lips; and another cautery pour the juice between .i. two breasts; and let the cauteries be called 'clavicle' according to the form that is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you see it, make cauterization in piercing all the cauterization that is called  'poins' from which the form is before in the disease of the ears; and let be the points up to .iii. or enqui entor. After cure the place according to what is before said, and let be the cauteries to .iij. rains according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for this reason the cautery is lighter, because you make it like this...
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, have the patient lie down on their back and on their left side; then heat the cautery to .iij. ners and apply it to the joint as follows:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the wound until it reaches the rib cage, and the form of the cauterization comes together with the cautery that has three nerves, because the nerve is according to the subtlety of a thread and this is the shape of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never apply to this one nerve because there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the fire cautery, treat with water; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated from above, let there be little pain, then apply cauterization to the thick cautery, or many cauterizations that pierce. Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is dried up, and the disease is cured.
dou cautere de pleuresin	To cure pneumonia.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	To treat pneumonia, they say one should use roots of arnica, and in this way: take a long root of arnica, the largest you can find, dry it, and make it as thick and long as your two hands; then soak it in oil, hold it over the fire, and cauterize. i.e., cauterize between the clavicle and the neck, and ii. small cauterizations a little down the side of the beard; and ii. cauterizations between the fifth and sixth ribs, by leaning back a little; and i. cauterization under the breast, and i. another over the stomach, and i. between the shoulders, and ii. small cauterizations from the back, away from the shoulder; and do not squeeze your hand, but make an open gesture as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	No older person said that anyone should use fire-like cauterization, and scratch and put it between the ribs, as much as it comes to the aphesis; and they say that one feels pain, as we have said in the aphesis of the liver. But in this chapter there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse of what we have said about the division of the treatments, and it does not benefit, then they devoted .ii. ways to cauterize that all are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	Of which there is one way such that you make .ii. cauterizations, or .iii., in according to the length of the mouse, in according to the shape of the fire cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the mouse be sore on his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cautery which has 10 ners, as we have demonstrated in the dislocation of the shoulder; and place the cautery where the mouse's cut comes from left to right, and let the elevatons that you feel where the mouse was cut be according to the length of his back, and the cauterization is according to the width of his back.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After that, the 10 ners are heated until the elevatons are felt from the other side, and then the cautery is taken away, and in doing so there will be .iii. ways. And if you see, then cauterize all of it with 10 ners. After the cure has been applied for a long time, and this will suffice that the other cure mentioned before is sufficient.
de ydropisie	about gout
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	For gout, except in the manner called "asclepiades." When you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned in the divisions, and your treatment is of no use, then you should do .iiij. cauterization around the boude, and .i. on the stomach, and one on the liver, and .i. on the kidney, and .ij. behind the back on the spine, and .i. on the testicles; and let the cauterizations be close to the cure.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, keep the cauterization in place for a long time, and do not remove the treatment from the patient after the cauterization; and with God's help, healing would be quicker, and both of the two intentions would come together with God's aid.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cauterization for the stomach is the one that we have mentioned before; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it has been described above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the fingers
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the fingers are swollen in a person who is ydropical, and they are plain yellow, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the index finger and the middle finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making 20 cauterizations on each leg at the tip of the toenail; and let the cauterization be long, one behind the knee in front and the other behind, with the leg; and leave the cauterizations for a long time without erasing, so that the awes are made; after curing the others we have said.
de la menoison	of the mansion
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution from the stomach comes from cold and moisture, as long as the virtues that retain and digest in the stomach and in the intestines are evaporated, and cannot be cured by any methods; and you see the patient very suffering and of great virtue, so it is done. i.e. a great cautery on the stomach according to what he has talked about here before or the cautery of the stomach, the cautery circulates; and 2.iiij. cauteries around the navel gently to all i. cautery nailed gently, and 15 cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abound and the patient is suffering, make cautery on the wrist, and 1 cautery on each finger, and 2 small cauteries on the stomach, for this cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
