de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the gangrene which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cope with gangrene, if you heat the cautery which seems sharp, and then put it all on fire on that gangrened coped; and leave it so that the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, where there is little movement; do this once or twice, and if there is more gangrene, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cures of beneficial herbs as long as they are healthy; and if you cauterize with a great cautery on alchatim, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound badly cured
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate surgery or opening, which we will describe in detail, if there is a disease that cannot be cured except by fire cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is a fistula present, and it has become inflamed and has pus and moisture, if the disease can be completely cured with a precise cauterization, and you know exactly how much cauterization is needed; after that, warm the fire instrument which seems sharp, and dip it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and restart the fire as many times as the amount of pus and corrosion that needs to be burned, once or twice or three times according to the quantity of the need; and be careful with the nerves that are in those places, and do not burn them unless they are furred; believe that they are not persisting; after that, cure those places until they are completely healed, and if the matter is not osteized [hardened], know that the disease has been cured entirely; and if the matter is osteized [hardened] at its base, know that the disease has been burned three-quarters of the way, and the bone has been corrupted at its base; and thus as one of these that we will describe in detail.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When there is pain in the kidneys, and a loud windiness, and it does not respond to women's remedies, then you must cauterize the kidneys from both sides with the clove-shaped fire instrument which we have described above; and if we cauterize them in the middle, there will be 2 [cloves] of fire on each side, and it will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to lack of urine and moisture, so that the patient retenes urine, then do a fire cautery in the region below the bladder, where the hair of the genitals encumbes, and so on both sides, and each cautery be as long as a finger; and do a cautery behind the back, where you need it; and let the cauteries be carved according to the form described above.
de la marris	of the mare (horse)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their season is delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: so it is necessary to do 11 cauteries in the region of the womb, as we have said in the bladder cautery, and 9 cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be carved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hips
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip box, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints are found in the department of the viscera, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip box at .i. a fire cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the joint around the box as it turns, so that the box is inside the circle; and if so, let the cautery be such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make 3 large olive oil cauterizations, and let the cauterization be also perfect as all the others; and the cure until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hips
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip of the leg, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division [of treatment], and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purify the patient of the large humors with pills made from rotten substances, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery, and the method of the cautery is according to .ij. methods: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to mout de ways, from which one is such: that you cauterize on the hip of the leg  .iij. triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a deep and large one, and between each cautery leave a space the size of a thumb, and let them be olive-colored; never do you make a cautery in the middle on top of the head of the hip, for there are  .iiij. according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cautery at the cautery of the circle that we have just said before in the dislocation of the hip; but make it in such a way that the circle contains all the hip, and all the space of the wound is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method that we do in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach until the thigh or leg; and if it comes only until the thigh and leg, then you make   .ij. cauteries where the patient says that the pain holds, and   .i. cautery on top of the ankle  .iiij. times, a little to one side: and let the cauteries be scalpel-like, and let the thickness of the wound burn; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or near the ankle, then you cauterize at the place where he feels the pain   .iij. points or   .iiij. according to the cautery that is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he is a man of trade, he does so much the better; and if he feels that the pain comes from the knee towards the thigh, he makes a cautery with a cuttle or circular knife, and you must take great care in all your cauterizations not to leave any of them so long as they are burning, and that you do no greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I have seen many who have made a cautery on the sole of the foot and left it so long that the leg was completely gone, and even the bones, and it became perverted and corrupted all the way through. After a dissolution of the entrails, which killed him.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in each one, according to this way. // And the wise said in the cautery of the ankle, that it is the manner, make a piece of iron and be at the head as well thick as a nail of finger, or a little less, and be between the intertruses and also from the one intertruse to the other space the quantity of a nut of nail; and let the intertruses be over of two parts, and are also like nails, and there is each piece of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated so that it is all red and put on, and then put it on the box of the bad ankle, and turn it on the lower back rib; and the cautery once 1 cautery burn and leave 2 days; and then make plaster with oil, and let the wound open long time; after the cure of ointment until it is well.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its smell, and few use it; but this is a good cautery which can bear it, and where it afflicts.
de la dolor dou dos	of the two
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from rubbing or from impact or from too much evacuation, or from the appearance of expanded cold matter, no one of these appearances is worth a cure, except that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is appropriate that after this person has voided the foul pills or other things, one should apply to his back, where the pain is, three lines of three inches long, and in each line make the cauterization according to the cauterization which is called "poins"; and if you see, make 1.5 cauterizations or 2.0 at the clavicle cauterization according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Maitre, many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of trouble are that they have a tight spine when they stand up and are afraid; and you find in the back of the neck and in us the appearance that comes on the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this, and when you have healed it, cauterize it with fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the fire is equally red hot on each part of the spine; and if you see it, cauterize it with fire piercing 10 or 15 lines, and let the points be close together. After curing it, as long as it remains healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not use the fire in girder-making which is made of nerve-spines.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the joints ache because of moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in pieces, which the doctors properly call "rheumatism," and when it is a cold cause and cannot be cured with medicine, then it is cured by cauterizing in this way: make the fire cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the olive cautery follow this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	When it is necessary to strike at the root of the foot, make a fire cautery on all the cauterization that one claims "point." And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make a cautery on each knee with three cauterizations or four on each part, following the whole olive cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold the fire hard except when the root of the pain is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend up to the knees and back, administer the cautery that we have spoken about in our chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make 16 points around the knuckles; and if there remains any pain in the two joints, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and govern the patient well and give him medicines. For if you do this well and purify the flux, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the syrup
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in anger, and the bowels descend to the loins and is new, so it is necessary that when you look at him to cure, he does not hurt him that day; and use things that leave his belly, so that the end descends from his belly; after this let him sit on his back between your hands, and order him to wash his hair as long as the bowels are repaired, and bring them to your sides, and sign of a half-circle above the navel with one hand; then heat the cautery where there is this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	as soon as the bowels come down to the loins and is new, so it is necessary that when you look at him to cure, he does not hurt him that day; and use things that leave his belly, so that the end descends from his belly; after this let him sit on his back between your hands, and order him to wash his hair as long as the bowels are repaired, and bring them to your sides, and sign of a half-circle above the navel with one hand; then heat the cautery where there is this form:
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you come up to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to their measure, and that of old people also great according to their measure; after iii days cure his hair with oil as long as he is healthy, and make him lie down for 40 days on his back as long as the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his rinsings be refreshed for a long time, so that the bowel does not come out when he goes to bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after .xl. days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage, and change it every .xl. other days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against too much drinking and eating, and against too loud yelling; and when he does this teaching, then he is completely cured. And I will say here later the cure of the barber in his chaplet.
de la routure dou ventre	Of a rupture from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, make the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let the third be cured; after the cure according to what we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at the cautery's three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but the first sign is the top of the belly and make a line on its width over the rupture, and another behind, and your hand all around the whole cautery; But the first cauterizations are lighter and more tender.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, or of sitting or of hurting, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary that he be burned at the fire called "poins", and let the burnings be according to the length of the member and its smallness and its feebleness and its virtue and its location from twists and its pain. If he is cured with the first burning, it is good; otherwise, begin another burning on that one, for such a custom is that it must move to the member that is nearest, so that you must make the burnings until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	of meals
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	of meals
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if he feels pain everywhere, and it becomes obvious, then you should cauterize him with these cauterizes that we have described at the head, i.e. cautery in his nose, and ii cauteries on the spine of the neck, and vii cauteries on the spine of the back, and i great ones on the skull, and another delight on the shoulder, and ii cauteries on the shoulders, and ii cauteries on the sides, and ii cauteries on the bones of the hand, and on the pits of the hands; and guard against the nerves that are under his feet, so that you do not burn them, and never make any cautery on the bone of the knuckle, nor another on the bone of the stomach, nor another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I make cauterizes, the more I help and benefit him; and know that the patient does not feel pain at the cauterize as much as a healthy person feels it, because his body is already very corrupted. And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the form of iron. After curing him, let him eat flour of times with honey and other cures until he is healed.
de enfleure	of
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When the swelling comes in any member and is cured by medicines and oils and poultices, and it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little entering into the flesh of the cure; then heal with ointments until it is healed. And never do cauterization and hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that silences the member, and thus if it is osted the swelling; and nevertheless does not interfere if he is not familiar with members and outlets of moving nerves.
de albaras	of defenses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awake, and the medicine does not help, then cauterize with a fine cauterizer according to the size of the flesh, until the blotch is osted and its color changes; then cure with flour and lentils, mixed with roasted oil and plantain leaves, and wormwood and almonds, each in parts; and mix them all together, and bind them with a cloth, and apply them to the affected area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	For the cure of leperous disease by fire
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the sore begins to appear, and you keep your eyes open, if you cauterize it with a cautery which seems a circle, go all around the edge of the sore. And yet, there are those who say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the sore; and yet, I do not think this is good, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it done before; and it is better that it be cauterized all around, with a cautery called "circular", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the fever which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it takes a long time to die or because of the excess of blood that it makes or because of the age of the sick person when he is very old and has little blood, or because of the heat of the disease when he is very hot, and you see him hastening to die: then cauterize him all around with small cauterizations by poking; after which let him be. For she will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you pierce her all over with the cautery, making the cautery very hot, then:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterization has not finished healing, and make it such a cauterization that the patient feels relief in one way or another so that the course of the corruption is chosen. After the cure until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of a disease called "corrodens", and is no more than a member putrefaction, for it corrupts the members as the fire dries them up. If you see this disease in its early stages and can use cauterization with fire, then heat the nails carefully, large and small, according to what suits the place of the disease; after cauterizing all around until you have removed all corruption, and nothing remains but the corroded members themselves, which are burnt up by the fire. And then leave it for .iij. days, and put oil on the cauterized places so that the burns from the fire heal, and all corruption is removed. After the oil cure, if health does not return after .iij. days, start again the cauterization on those which are still corroded. And this putrefaction is never cured with medicinal oil instead of fire cauterization; but fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already spoken about the cure with medicinal oil in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of radishes which come from the ground
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mouth of times there is that the hairs by default grow a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a gross thing seeded which bleeds the foot. And the cauterizations of this disease are as follows: .ij. ways. That is to say, fire cauterization, and water cauterization. Fire cauterization is such that you heat up .i. cauterization tool like a vulture's beak, and it must be made of good iron in the measure that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and it has fine margins; then place it all hot on the nail, and bring your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the base; and leave it so .iij. days until it starts to rot; then make an ointment of wild mallows crushed with water, and leave the ointment on all night, and let the nails dry up and will be rooted from their roots. Then cure the wound with salt as much as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if the body is converted by default, and many times are put on hands and feet, it is appropriate that you bring fire cauterization; and this is a third way: take an iron or metal wire, or a vulture's beak, and place it on the nail and the athelous part, that is to say, make warts; then place the wire on so that it bleeds all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the margin of the wire comes to the base of the nail, and can find the deep path of hot water until the root; and let the patient feel a little the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will be rooted from all its roots. In this way do one after another, until you have removed all those that are in the body, then cure the wounds with salt as much as they are healthy.
li cure dou trembler	And cure the shaking.

des pustules puans	For the pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	For the pus-filled blisters that appear on the body, which come from corrupt substances, it is necessary to make a cauterization on each bump: a thin cauterization made with mugwort, which is held in the fire, or with the root of aristo, or with the lenticular cauterization. And it is not necessary to do this at the very beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow any further, but are broken up and healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	For when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Maitres doctors, I pray you to hear my words and to pay attention to the advice that I am about to give on this most important of topics. For there are many times when a great deal of trouble can come from the blood in the arteries, which comes out onto the skin when cutting into an abscess or cauterizing a limb, and similar things; and it is a terrible thing to smell.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Many times there is great trouble from the blood in the arteries, which comes out onto the skin when cutting into an abscess or cauterizing a limb, and similar things; and it is a terrible thing to smell. And you must do this: when one of these happens, immediately put your index finger on the vein, and strain it until the blood stops flowing from the wound with your other hand, and do not allow any drops of blood to fall; then take some olive oil, small or large as the wound requires, and heat it thoroughly until it is completely red; then dip  .i., that is, a cotton swab, a piece of wool, or a piece of cloth into the hot oil, and hold it over the vein at which you are holding your finger, or where you are holding your finger, and keep the oil in place until the blood has stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds when you lift your finger from the vein, and the oil has cooled, then quickly take another swab, or a piece of wool or cloth, dipped in hot oil, and hold it over the place where you lifted your finger until the bleeding stops.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood has stopped; and be aware that you should not burn the nerve which is delicate, and that no other harm should come to the patient; and know that when the artery has been cut, it cannot be well healed unless one of the four ways that we have said is used: or by cauterizing, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying it, or by putting medicines on it which have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and held tightly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer a hot poultice closely wrapped around the wound or place burning things upon it, or other similar things, unless he does so to no avail?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Who will administer a hot poultice closely wrapped around the wound or place burning things upon it, or other similar things, unless he does so to no avail? If there is no medicine or remedy present, one must place his index finger upon the edge of the wound as we have said, and hold it firmly over the wound and the edge; and do not move it, but wet it often with cold water until the blood is frozen and thick and solid; and make incisions in front of the area where cauterization and medicine are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds. We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases where fire cauterization, or burning medicine, and the methods, causes, tools, and shapes of cauterizations are needed; and I have placed that chapter at the beginning, and I will go on from there in this chapter by that same path for those who wish to heal more lightly than those who desire it.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, oh man, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauterices, and for this reason it is necessary to be more cautious.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to take any foolish actions. For such things often come from people who, because of the severity of their illness and the greatness of their wickedness, die easily due to the mischief that their disease brings about, and because of the great evil in their illness; and for this reason one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of those who have such a way of thinking, who say: "Wait, I am going to die"; and the disease is spiteful. It is not good that you consent to such people who come to you who have this manner; but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not open your doors foolishly but carefully confirm what you are certain of, and what you may have taken from him; and use prophecy and indication when treating your sick, so that health may be converted; and he who will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:

dou chief plein d’aigue	Here is the final sentence for you to translate. Please provide your own translation if you would like me to compare it to mine or if you would like to see it in another format:
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and all those that I have seen die quickly; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better to delay the work of this chapter in the treatment.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child where the head was swollen with water, and each day it swelled more until he could not support his own weight; and because of the moisture it came to be as if dead, and this moisture, so gathered around the bone under the skin, between the skull and the bone; and the work of this chapter, so is this moisture gathered around the bone under the skin, and the abscesses are small, that you cut a wide slit in the head at the top; and be also as far apart as possible, so that the moisture runs; and see here the form of the spetumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, then make two slits in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is outside the bone, and the signs that you see are the folds of the skin on either side, and when you press it with your hand from the inside, there is no response; then cut three slits in the form of this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture. After drawing out the bandages and powders, pour wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then unbind it, and cure the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head be drawn out evenly, and give the patient dry meat soaked in a little moisture until the member is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to incise is that you look at the opening of the aposteme, and the joining of the astringent; for it is never before; never behind; never on the right; and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So size it accordingly, and fill it according to your ability, and beware that you do not plug the artery; and bring forth blood, so that the patient may die of thirst and due to the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of remedy
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a person has a disease called "cataract" in the eye or in the knee, and the disease is old, and medicine does not benefit him, then the next treatment is to cauterize with that which covers the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	When the person's eyes are covered with a film, and the disease is old, and medicine does not help him, then, when you peel back the skin, the patient should rub his head with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, and then extract the patient's tongue to all 1/4th of a cloth; then look where the vein goes, and their necks are both on the sides of their ears, and they have been torn; then sign the necks with one and the other of two spatulums that are sharp at both ends, as far as the bone comes out, and this one is done by the large side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, you should remove the blood vessel with the spatulum and cover it on top, cutting it like two sides with two spatulas at the same time.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is covered, let it continue to flow upward without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et si le sang ne sort pas au toucher, il convient que tu mesures la quantité de l'espace de .iij. doses, puis signe d'encore et fente jusques à l'os; et celui que il convient de mettre de sang est vj c/, et par aventure un peu plus ou moins. selon ce que le malade peut souffrir, et la repletion de l'artere; puis regarde la plaie: s'il reste sur l'os point d'écoulement, si le cope que apostèmes chaus n'i veigne, puis estrange la plaie et lie, et la cure d'oignement tant qu'elle soit guérie.
de emigrainne	And if the blood does not flow upon touching, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of 3 doses, then sign to stop and cut as far as the bone; and that which is to be put of blood is vj c/, and by chance a little more or less. according to what the patient can bear, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone no drainage, if the plug that absces chaus does not come out, then extrude the wound and bind, and the cure of ointment as long as he is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient migraine comes, and catarrh acquired, because of the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old feverish and similar things, and it is medicated by the methods of medicine and all that does not benefit him, then we extrude the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, if as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patient should grow his hair on his temples again, and feel the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and is not much filled except in some people who are too cold; and if it is filled, then remove its neck with some drapes, then rub its place with any rough cloth, and raise the place of hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula where there is this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	And then peel the skin slightly until you feel the artery, and then turn it up like pincers, and completely remove the webs that are attached to each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it into a point with the hook, and then cut off that part according to the quantity of .ij. degrees. Because if it is not cut, then there will be no saving of anything at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And turn the blood of 1/4th to 1/3rd, and if the artery is large, then tie it with a double strong silk thread, that it not be broken before the wound's healing; then cut off the excess that is between the 2 threads at that moment as well, and then, if you see, then cauterize with fire from the cautery knife until the bone is reached, and this is the work of the surgery, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cautery is an aid to finish off the moisture: for this is a greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Ou il convient por l'extraction des arteres que om remplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu'il soit sanez; et se sans court de l'artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l'estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n'as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d'aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il convient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l'extraction de l'artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cet cautere trenchant de  .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too soft, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And should have between the .ij. tools a .i. inch of space, and then when you have cut into the .ij. veins, and you measure with the sharp edge on top until it reaches the bone, and cap the voice in .ij. veins; and they are separated between the .ij. shoulders because it is not softened by this cautery from all sides; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes run down into the veins that are under the skin of the head of force, and the medicine I make does not benefit him, and you see the face of the sick person turn black, and feels a cold movement as if it were frost; and since they are kept and moist so that the hairs of the papers fall, and the papers get burned and scalded by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it the "old cure", and that is what you do to the sick person whose hair is at the front, then make .iij. cuts at the front equally long; and one of the cuts be as much as .ij. two all along the front up to the nose, and the other .ij. two at the sides over the papers, and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .ij. mandibles, and each wound have the quantity of .iij. dos;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and then put on a piece of sponge and soak it with the water of the springs, then pour the sputum out from the two parts where this form is;
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile. si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	"And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady..."
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady and keep them still until you reach the middle cut; and if they prick again, hold them steady again until you reach the other side; then remove the sharp edge and express the blood; then put a piece of fine cotton cloth in each cut, and cover it with wet linen dipped in wine and oil and mustard, and make sure that the feet don't come into contact with it; and on the third day unbind him, and apply a great amount of cold water, then apply the basilicon ointment with oil of roses, and other cures for wounds, until he is healed."
dou reume des eulz	"And then remove the sharp edge..."
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When there is no catarrh coming by custom, and you see the hairs drawn back and small, and the vision weakens, and the paper burns; and the hair is scattered, and where it chief hurts a pain, and the patient coughs; then know from these accidents that those matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure that is for them, if it is this, so it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And so you command the patient to rub his forehead, then make a wide cut across the forehead, and another large incision from side to side; and start from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, and cut all the way down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples that move when he drinks; and when the bone is exposed, then wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then tie cotton wool and linen thereon; then lay wet cloths in wine and oil, and beware of an abscess; when it is exposed, so you must rub the bone until the char begins to be born, then cure it with dry things, which cause chaps.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take .iiij. parts of flour of rice, and .iii. parts of kollofyn, and make a plaster therewith; and apply it to these wounds in order to produce chaps everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stiffening of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All who have ears are of the four things: or grain, or beast, or stone, or similar thing as iron; or seed, as peas and beans; or flowing thing like water and easily moving and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	For when it chills in the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not fit into the ear, nor does it grow in the ear, so put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, then pour a drop of violet oil or seed oil; then it is extracted, and the work is to shake it, and the nose stops when the shaking comes, and puts cloth or wool pieces behind the ear; and raises the ear up. Many times this cure comes; and if it does not come, it is extracted with gentle pincers, from which there is this form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the pincers, it is good; if not, then extract it with a small double hook; and if it does not jump out with that, make a chain of raindrops and put the end of the chain or a small passageway in the ear very hard, and stop what is inside with soft wax so that it cannot enter with the chain; then try to force it, because many times it comes like this as we have said; and if it does not come out in any way, take glans from it, and put cotton in some tool which is right for what you want to do, and put a drop of cotton; then press the glans on the stone or whatever it is, and try to force it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not jump out with any of these things that we have said, then cut the ear so that the aposteme is split, and spasms; and the way to cut it is that you first extract the disease from the head of the skull, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue, then put the sick person between your hands and turn their ear up, and make a small cut at the root of the ear with grease or something hanging; and let the cut be as the moon, until you touch the stone, then press it according to your strength, and suck it gently into your mouth; and the cure until they are well.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that has become damp and begins to swell, extract it; and if it cannot be extracted, make a thin paste of it according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision in the grain but do not make it when you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them carefully and finely with a blade and add to the syrup, as we said, so that the extractions are ordered.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	So that the patient uses sneezing with condiments first and wipes the ear with old cotton. And be careful on which ear he has fluid. If it is, it's good. If not, take many little stones according to the length of your finger and make them hot on the fire; and put one or two of them in his ear, and pull them out from the other side, and take another stone from the ear that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with a stone in an ear until all the fluid has come out, and so it comes out completely; and if you see, take a piece of straw, and bottle one of the ears, and the other ear take fire from the straw, as we said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the best, if it is a small worm, such as a flea or similar thing, cure it as we said in the division; but if it is a large one that can be felt, make an incision with a blade; and this is the lightest thing to extract from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where we treat the distillations, and the cure does not profit, if it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun: if there are no worms, take the pinches softly, and if they do not appear, take the hair of where it is the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And be tight below and wide above. And pour the subtlest chief into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck all the way; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, if you break in with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not rise up as we have said, administer distillations which the old ones have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them where we treat the distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, where it is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be tight below and wide above. And make a small hole for distillation with an instrument of silver or gold, and press it above to distil; and to squeeze the distillation into an instrument of silver very well made for sucking, and if you see that you have taken a razor and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and what you want of your medicines in the hair, and let the hair be in the ear; then pour the oil into the razor with all the cotton, and press your hand firmly so that the oil is distilled from the ear; and have the patient smell it, and let the distillation burn slightly at the fire as we do when we distil in the ear; and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the sticking up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a piercing in their ears; and this same thing happens to men due to an upward movement of the ear, or a horse's hoove inside it, and such a piercing often comes all the way into the ear if one cannot see it; and there is no piercing of the ear,
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then let the ear of the patient face the sun; and look inside: if you see the operation become apparent, then that is all this spice has done to it:
