Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and I pour one thread twisted in two, and I plug the tent in all the thread in the ulcer as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is persistent at the base inside, then extract the thread of that torn, so you plug your two or base foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and join together the two heads with thread, and hold them apart from each other, and leave them for one day or for two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not restrain it once, until the thread holds these joints together that are between two, and they grind;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is souded and healed over.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you can pierce it in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too completely hidden.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make a covering bandage without first making the wound perfect, and then treating it, as we have said, until it is well.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spikelet from which one makes a fistula is sharp and has a point; part it and cut through it.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	And on the other hand, for this reason one should not cover with a bandage what one must not cover, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Here is the translation of the provided text:
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and some have one or more, and those that are distant from the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are distant have little moisture, and
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and then cut close together or a little apart, or a little water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh; and
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those who have them within the foundation, so you command the patient that he defecates in bed until the foundation goes away and it comes out; and
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and hold it with your fingernail, then cut it into its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if his nail does not hold them because of the moisture, then take them from the .i. drapeil, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and remove them with your two hands, then cut them, and powder them with any hot powders that are in the fire of cauterization;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization with chapister (a kind of substance), then treat them with other treatments until they are healthy again;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if his foundation cannot come out, then cauterize the patient with a hot cautery, and sharp, so that it washes what is at the foundation, so that it can come out freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	When the patient has been burned, and his hair is burned away from his foundation, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you should hold them in your nail or with tweezers, and pull them out, then cure them as we have said, until they are well, and avoid the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you bring the stitch together in this way: take a twisted thread, and put it through an needle, and then draw the thread up from the bottom of the needle, and push the needle through the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread over the needle
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is a large one; then draw out the thread, and tie it, and take out the needle, and do so with all of them, and leave only one . i . for drawing away the surplus blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then wrap it in a cloth wet with oil or wax, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it bleeds, and when it stops bleeding, if he is cured with ointment and other cures, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Douiciously at the end of the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying up of the ends in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no good.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you should come to the point of a scalpel or your fingernail on top, which does not leave it to moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it as soon as it is sore, as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be healed, then shave it more strongly than before, until it heals and is scorched;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat him until he is well.
dou fremit	the sweat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	is a small brown stain on the skin, and goes well with much of the dress;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and it does not hurt the patient at all, and one can feel it even through clothes, and comes throughout the whole body, and especially to the hands compared to elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an owl or a strong vulture, and place that feather on the wound, until the purple ring surrounds the entire wound.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand around all the feather until you have surrounded the wound completely, and place it in place, and then clean the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you want to make a cautery with fire or iron according to this form, and be careful not to burn yourself, and do it slowly.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not cut, but rather pinch between your fingers, and press: And if you want to cauterize the wound, as it is described in front or with cauterizing chapiter.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cyst
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one should make silver or mercury enema, or melted gold or brass; and no one should use these small or large instruments according to those who are treated.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, for the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, these are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cyst is small and large if it is over the belly, or tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and I saw one distension where the belly is tied, so that you see it, and the ribs are pierced from within; and at one of the sides there is .ij. perforations, and on the other side .i..
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly be filled with a capsule of honey or parchment, and let it be pierced all around the small openings.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each opening, place 1/10th of a space, then pour in these openings a strong twine made of cow's intestine, and tie the belly together as if it were a sheep.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if the string is in front of a strong instrument, then cauterize it; and it takes on the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil of olive or of castor oil or a similar substance, then pour it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	and the minister holds them together with his two hands until it is completely full, then remove the oil, and raise the patient's legs to the wall,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and let the medicine flow out, as much as he can; and if he sleeps all night, it is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize him because of a disease that comes from the inside of the belly, and the medicine flows out quickly, if he goes back to the same thing as often as he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or abscess, then also the clister is too thin like a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the clister that is too thin so that the skin is held back:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the cure of wounds; but now we will speak of the cures of hands and medicines, according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and because of this they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Things that cause wounds are by the slitting of a stone, and the hewing of an axe or a knife or a spear or a lance or a fust or a sledgehammer or similar objects; or
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or where the body parts are cut according to their places, such as a wound that bites into the neck, or the head, or the side, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the reminder will come in my chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound appears where the head is, and the bone is not broken, take care that it is from the movement of stones or similar things, and the skin is torn everywhere, and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the burning of an abscess: if you do not quickly heal from blood loss caused by the wound, and you heal on the opposite side of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and you prevent the patient's replenishment with wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not quickly heal, if his meat is reduced, and he does not drink wine or eat cheese;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and over the wound, if it is a hot sore, cotton wetted with oil of rose, or with wine as astringent;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if it is not a hot sore, and over the wound, if it is fresh, without moving with the air, powder, which I will call a little further on;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it has been moved, and over some herbs, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, as long as a sword blade and similar things, and the lips cannot be put together by tension, if they are put together by sewing, as I will say to wounds on the belly, from the sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone and there is little blood, then bandage the wound with cloth only, and return it to its place.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat large, solid foods, such as roasted meats, grains, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rottenness in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut it off completely and throw it away, and then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which, without stopping, and he cannot stop it with medicine, then find the artery, and if you find that it is dislocated, then bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not benefit him, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light cure is: and that you put this powder which hardens so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the way of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood .ij parts; live coal .iij parts, and the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and the bandage forms, as long as it dries well and sticks to all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it unhindered if it does not swell, for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time does one use salt at all, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but that the arm does not move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arm has moved the wound, even a little, one must then use this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some oil infusions that have been prepared, or peas of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it is warm;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the doctor prescribes other remedies until he is cured.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with gentle tweezers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you this afterward about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the throat
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the neck and is simple, there is no difference between it and that at the base of the head, but if the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is at the base, then there is no other remedy but to leave it alone and not put anything restraining on it, for it harms the base and makes it retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the base is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but either make the medicine hot, as hot water in mild water, and mixed with rosewater, and also wash it with mild water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones from my body according to this method, and oil with moisture.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the bandage is too loose, then treat until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	If the wounds are deep and the hair is shaven and full of bowels, if the wound or deeper;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and pain in the heart comes, if the darkness, and the fever, and the cauterization is necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the throat is closed, or a hole made there, and the direction is kept, so that the meat goes down.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if the hole is cut high up on the neck, and does not touch the throat but sets it back to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then let it rest for a few days, and then treat it with oregano until it is well again;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has affected the bone, then rub it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, if you can't handle them all, and those that you can't have, let the wound rot.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful and firm with the issue;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I said in my chapter on the chapistle.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then examine the wound to see if there are any signs of life in it: know that such a wound is deadly.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it isn't deep and the wound is fresh, then in the first hour don't apply powder or bandage to the wound that wouldn't hold it in place until it heals perfectly.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and rest, and take care of the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I have a remedy for this, and the leech 13 times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have a wound, put wet cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient lie on the wound 13 times, or 23 times, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there will not be a spasm, nor a malevolent tremor of the heart from which no remedy is found;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see such good arrangements, know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds of tents and other cures, as long as he is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and if surgery is necessary, then know that there is a fistula; and if the cure is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is made with a knife or sword, and it is simple, or deep or at the back, then know how to heal what is before it;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, use sutures; and if it is small, use powder, and if it has penetrated the bone, and split it into pieces, then treat the wound, and if they have become infected.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not infected, then allow the wound to fester, and then perform extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	and the rupture of the womb
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the womb is great and painful and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From a great wound does not come once the intestines, or the intestines go into one another, for this is the introduction of pus.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	And the suture is more difficult, and there is no benefit from a small wound compared to a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	For if we do not put the intestines back together again, we should put them back together piece by piece;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	for this reason the intestines swell so that they feel cold, if they return to their base,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason the wound is closed, so that it heals well, if we keep the intestine in place as with the others
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the abdomen is according to three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common seams have in the seam of the abdomen,

Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestines with water or brew them, and if the spicing is cooked,

que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we do not cut it unless there is a great need;for for this cause li chapistre est plus usé, par ceu qu’il peut faire venir la sanglerie de ses membres, et que li malaides sent le douleur moins;

si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If it breaks in towards the corbière and doesn't go out, and see the form:

Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the belly,

Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds but also this

et assemble les levres;	and gather the lips together.

et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you twist a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,

et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles fall, between fine and coarse,

k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;

car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it needs a needle or .ij.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second method of sewing is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and are joined together with a strong thread that cuts easily;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have perceived these things together,

ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is for the king,

Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the nine proper ways to stitch:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and thread it from the outside part all the way inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When she has bitten the hook of justice, if you have twisted or pulled out the needle

et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the hook on one side, and pick it up on the other, until the stitch is completed entirely.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galiens performed properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is if so that as any font, who assemble the .ij. parties together naturally,

de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bole

si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one can restore it in some way,

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	is called "fistula" universally when it has come to light.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most often when it has been cut and a bow has been made.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And the fistula is according to the vertue of the hard and white nodulation, or there is no pain felt,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also like a bird's beak;

aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and never pokes, but is enough.

Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The fire cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two of you should work together so that the baby is born in a man's hands; by chance it may be all flesh.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is some bone there and no nails,

The process of fusing together the two pieces of linen is known as "sewding", and it is done with the palms of the hands, as is customary. Des vils	The evil ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The evil ones are huge envelops filled with excessive melancholy that come from the limbs of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more are found in the legs of those who walk on their feet and work and carry things, whereas others...
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not at any time take any kind of medicine that makes the bowels move, and then heal from the Basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron according to the following 19 ways: one is that you make the cups, and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way is if you find the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting according to this method: arise the first leg with very hot water until the large vein is visible,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	and then strain the leg of the sick person from above the knee to the part near the ankle joint;

puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	and then draw out and pull firmly the black blood from your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it, and instruct him to dye his meat with black wine;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and then start the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are empty, and leave the patient.

De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance happens elsewhere than in the legs, and this is due to the porridge that comes off the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes into the body twisting and turning, slip between skin and flesh.

si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	then let it all out; and if the matter inside is empty, and place at its location remedies for inflammation any day, then treat it as for abscesses.

et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it causes a great wound, and from which there comes much blood; then treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that come between the hide and the meat
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	this disease is called in our country "bovine disease", because it often affects cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that grows between the hide and the frame, and goes up and down all over the body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it smells bad at the end of the limb where it went, and it jumps away furiously;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is infected with some kinds of fluids, like pus, blood, or other substances, and it is infested with worms or insects that crawl or swim;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and there is doubt about its malignity, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	In case of accident, destroy the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being cured and extracted, he can only be done so once:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So it is necessary that you place him on a firm bed with a very tight strap:
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then cut him from top to bottom and tra lui further, and the blood will run completely into the pan, and you will not find it:
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery is applied, until he dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does, if it corrects oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the oil, hold back the arm in a straight line, then swing up and throw it hard;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and use the medicine of purification with soluble medicines for the bad humors that may cause disease;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and se warse of meats janranc-porriture.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and moves from limb to limb; and I saw the one which I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her breast, and I saw a small swelling on the breast.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and I then saw it grow larger like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	much faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain leaves the body part, and settles in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it corrupts throughout the whole body, until it comes to the other side of the breast.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he told me that she twisted repeatedly in her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how much she moved her limbs from one member to another, for I have never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I have often heard that people with this disease suffer great pain from one limb to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not want it, if as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman had a dry chest, and the veins uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason it appears that she has constricted windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and does not appear to these who are delicate, and who have moist chests and uncovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you have cured this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the limb is raised and firmly supported, and then held in place until the wind is stopped.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see the blood stop,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of this disease, which stops the wind, as if it were pills of putrid garlic, and pills of serapint, and similar things.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the places of the body where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of them is such that there are some with large points, and others with small, and some with hair, and some welded.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with .ij. (20) angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those who bite in any member so according to .iij. ways: or in a principal member bit,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she bites in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary for you to wash yourself of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after a few more preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when there is no sign of badness yet, and the arrow is not fully extracted if it has gone in, then treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow bites and pierces the bone, and the medicine that is on the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a shock and a sudden turn and a rash on the skin, and inflammation and a rash on the tongue, and muscle spasm and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and it may be that there is no breath through the nostrils or ears; and it may be that speech or voice is lost.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the moist wound there comes white pus resembling blood, and also like smoke rising.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign shows that if you continue with the treatment, and bind the arrow if it is not stuck yet.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	For the sign of the arrow when it hurts or stings, it is close to the left breast, and also seems to be lodged in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if by chance the arrow also resembles blood, and dark black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat comes, and fainting occurs:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then come doubt that death will come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not burn is that there is no foam from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's complexion changes, and he sighs heavily and feels cold fear.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters the back, then it hurts the small ribs; and there is great pain and sighing; and all the limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters the stomach, perhaps there is no flesh hurt from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow lodges in the belly, and it does not go out through the intestine, then there is no hope for the cure or for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine comes out with a gush and goes away, and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and neck and throat and shoulder and ajutoire and spine and chest and legs and limbs are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the neck or artery, and it does not poison, then as I will tell you what happened to me, do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was a man who had an arrow stuck in his thigh at the root of his groin.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and cut off the fat of the ear from both sides, and was healed without any sense of pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I tried another arrow, which went into his thigh, cutting through the fat of the oil from both sides, separating the paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was withdrawn, and I only felt the tip go into his flesh.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and this arrow is great of a turquoise arch, to all that is to say lighter than ears; the game was healthy, and no bad accident came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And threw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and this arrow was Arabic to the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loved the barbs, and hid them well, and they were healthy for the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And threw an arrow at a man, which went through his cheek or belly, and I thought he died;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then he passed .xxx. days, if not he changed his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and set it in place, and tied it tightly, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a home with an arrow through it or a hole in its wall, and the wound is sewed up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and hold the arrow within it, and do not change its natural state,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	There is no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I see another man, to whom he shot an arrow in the face and it was sewed up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained there without suffering much pain; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And there was a sword given to a prince's man, the king, which had been broken on his neck;
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely pulled out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat after she had been injured for three days. The wound was very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I asked her to take a strong medicine, and I did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt pain and a ringing in her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought this was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on them the plaster with the attractive digestive juice, so that their leeches do not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the leeches of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on them the plaster every day, and quickly heals the wound, and holds back the disease for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he feels the arrow .i. within his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive medicinal ointment day by day, as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which had become firmly lodged;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I put on the wound in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow clearly appeared to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and well pass the limits of three months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then I cut the wound so that the nails came out, and pulled them with force from one side to the other, and could not draw them out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I stopped from devising and inventing means of instruments, until I had the nails well made;
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to this one that its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I have it cut, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I know that the cartilage of the nose cannot be healed.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I reset it then, and had it welded, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or I will tell you about the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your cure on what I have not said, for the book cannot include everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise men compare on very little thing, and on what is present and deficient,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	try nine or ten operation, and nine instruments to the removal of foreign things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not removed from the limbs except according to three ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either at the place where they enter or at another place;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps out from it, for where it enters, that is an arrow entering its flesh, and never leaps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it no longer leaps, leave the flesh to rot, and make clean the exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it thus for a few days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it leaps, and if it no longer leaps, pierce it from within with a sharp tool, as long as the flesh within is soft, and then treat it;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is embedded in the bone of the skull, and goes into one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said can happen to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it as long as it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if an arrow goes only as far as the sinus, death is certain.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if an arrow is embedded only in the bone of the skull, and does not go any further, it is certain death.
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains a few days without any bad accidents if the machine of pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is badly broken and cannot be taken out, then administer tar-water as I told you; then heal the joint as long as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in the chest so that it cannot be seen, and you want to find it with all your strength;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you can feel it, then use suitable tools;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by stretching the wound, and by the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	ne has neither bone nor nerve nor vein, so that the wound is as great as possible;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and if you can extract the arrow, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so that the bone is extracted by one-third of an inch from the muscle where you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or rain the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, but rather draw it out with pain.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, and the ear of the arrow is torn, then draw it out, for extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of the injection makes you reluctant, then administer what we have said in the chapter about the balm.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and warn against cutting through the nerve and the vein, and do not mention how one might remove an arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or hot or cold, or firmly or vigorously; and set the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow went in,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot do so, then set it according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens nothing, or the leather is swollen in a particular place, if we see or feel it appropriately:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Here is the translation of the text line by line into English:
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, as long as it enters into the bone and widens it, then remove it."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be removed, then let it go for a while, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out. "
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a arrow in it, pound it with all your strength;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it must be cut, and you see to administer poultices, for it will administer. I.e., the instrument is a scalpel
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hole of the instrument; and then pour out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is cut, pour out the instrument with a pointed end entering it, in order to celebrate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow touches, so that you cut all the skin around where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	and then heal the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow enters or is in the belly or bladder or side, and it is near, then you may cover it with a cloth, as it should be covered.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of covering the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, as is necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and heal it until it is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the claws for treating arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and this is how it should be done:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the claw at the end is also like the feathers of an owl.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	for bowing the tip of the arrow, as this is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of nails for holding and for keeping it in place thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one is healed are .xxxi., of which there is one at the head xvi.,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is what it means in English: It is known that: .iij. vessels are located behind the ears, which are called the two "herbeche"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 18 arteries that are in the 18 temples appear.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 18 veins that are in the 18 hairs of the 18, which are called "aspirations";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is under the forehead; and the vein that is on the top of the neck;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the 18 veins that are at the collar;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the 19 veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the 19 veins that are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly spoken of are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is the cephalic, and it lies on the left side, and it is called by the lay people "voinne du chef";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the name is called 'fast', and is composed of the cephalic and basilical.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it 'vein-cutter'; and if the basilical is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it 'vein-cutter in the belly', and is on the bright side,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is what is said about it: it opens clearly on the breast.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little finger is the one between the ring and the pinky, and if it has .ij. raindrops on it;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot are .iii veins: one is dislocated at the corner of the pocket on the left side of the calf,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are 3 veins dislocated from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The head pain of the veins that are behind the ears if it helps the old catarrh, and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the medicine, as I told you, is that you remove the head of the disease,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the leather where the veins are with an abrasive cloth; then strain the disease from his neck with a screw,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the .iij. veins appear behind the ears depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Keep the donkeys at two, and where you feel the chicken's pulse on your right side, if it is warm, it is a sign of good health.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lance and pierce through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand up towards the top of the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut off the skin and the flesh and the vein very carefully. Take two days to heal and rest.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then draw it out and wrap it up, so that it is healthy.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood vessels that are in the two temples, if they cause a migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and the eyes, and the nasals used to be affected, and in the shape of the larynx;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the patient is such that: I say it like this:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient pulls his neck out, as long as the .ij. veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and send a cold wind from his two feet, and then sign with pain on his throat;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	and place the ring finger of your right hand on the top of your index foot, and blow against it from below,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and place the vein on top, and the cup, as you have done in the .ij. other veins, and let the blood run according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then lay the patient down, and place two fingers on the vein for an hour, then cover with cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then let it form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about its joining and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the facial diseases of old, and for migraine and blindness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that if the patient twists his neck, so that the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip on the vein, and hold it firm in your hand or another object, and allow two drops of blood to flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then cut off the neck, and tie the vein until it is well and firmly tied, and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame must not be too hot; and the vein is cut across, for fear that the bone may break if the flame is too hot.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the two veins that are in the two eyelids should be let out, and with the eye, and with the fever, and with the yellowing of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their blood is that the patient should twist his neck out of any ligature, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the blood, and let it go through one little piece of a long flame, a little bit wide, for there is no fire;
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by accident if they break; then let the blood go out, as much as you need, and then tie it well on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The pain of the birth of the child is great if it is in water, and it is sudden, and the diseases of the face are great.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If it is a headache and a twinge that comes into the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of the pain so that the patient strangles his neck, then pulls his baby by the hand with his left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a thin long flame, and put it on the lip in the space between the iij. nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well here, and the blood will begin to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not make it too large, and make the blood run according to your need, then leave it for a night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	This is the form of the fire:
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of health is that the patient removes his hair from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient cuts off one side;
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein well and thoroughly, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then mend another in the other vein, then wash the neck and draw out the hair gently;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not choke; and leave him until morning, that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	of the health of the animals
