Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The surgeon should cut off the foot if he has any of the diseases that grow on the inside of the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	If, as a result of disease of the mare (horse), there is retention of flux (menstrual blood), and disease of the reins, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his health is such that the patient must drink cold water, and rub the vein until it stops.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot goes into the reins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	For the blood goes out at the bottom or wide place of the rain, or at the ankle, which must be held.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the leg, be careful of the nerves that are exposed, and treat it across as well as when it is in a cup; and let the fire fade away.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound cannot be brought out, put the leg into the water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is treated for the first time, start again for the second time above a little, because the blood is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle, and its pain goes to the hip, when it is for sciatica.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this pain is that the patient goes in or out, and pulls it off the ankle .iii. two in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so let the pain be in all ways that you can, and going through;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth more than you can cope with, for the leg is out, and it is very painful at hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not cure it, if there is no rain from him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the little day, and guard against the cold.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make so much blood go out that you see it, and then unstring the ligature, and put cotton on it and hold it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuum treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or of air, or of glass; and the treatment with the vacuum is done according to .ij. ways: either by hurting and drawing out blood, or not hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation which is not to hurt so it is according .ij. ways: or it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation that is made to hurt and to extract blood so it is done in 123 parts of the body
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	from which one is all on the top; and the other is half around the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and 2 others on 2 sides of the neck; and 1 at the bottom under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventose of the .ij. shoulders; and the ventose on the crups;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the ventoses emmy the .ij. arms; and the ventoses of the .ij. legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the ventoses of the .ij. ankles; and the ventilation does not treat of blood, unless it is that of small veins that are scattered throughout the carriage;
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore you do not fear any injury, if it is done like the treatment of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be amputated, nor with any fire or hot application in any disease that comes from over-fullness, as long as the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, because of the necessity of disease or habit, it is necessary to amputate, or because of a particular hour in the month, or at the end, and each one in turn;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they need to ventilate, become very heavy;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who, with the ventilation, have paleness and redness on their face and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who drink a drop of blood in their mouths, and have escaped the tongue, and yearn for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such people who dream and see, and feel pain, death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is mid-month, we order them to breathe out after .iij. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sage of the muse so helps with grief in the chest ... that it comes to the eyes, and does not come except after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in place of the health of the cephalic,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not come to anything that is of cold disposition in use, or who has chaturd (a word possibly related to "chatur" meaning "impure"), for this does them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because of that it does not come to anything that is of a cold disease in use, or who have or head cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are healed from it often become confused, and because of that the fire cautery should be put a little further down by the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventilation of the neck is at the level of the sinus of the head and the base of the skull, and for this reason it causes contraction of the muscle of the spine.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to a split in the channel of the windpipe, and all, and to filling up;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push back, for if it holds too tightly, there is danger of a chock or stomach or place.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilation of the neck is at the level of the sinus of the head and the base of the skull, and for this reason it causes contraction of the muscle of the spine.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the saint's bazaar; and it is necessary that you command the saint that he express his hand to put it on, that he does not cut the artery, and does not cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windings of the nose lead to disease in the mouth and decay of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the saints of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders lead to a disease that comes from heat and filling up.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The windings of the neck lead as much as the three veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon that he does not cut too deeply, for the arteries and veins are bare of hair, and it is easy to cut into them.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back so easily rips out the foundation, and the disease, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and of leather, because it has to milk well; and by chance, if it were too thin, it would break; and it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs so easily rip open, for they draw blood from the entire body, and resemble ancient pains of the legs, and of the hip, and of the knee; and they weaken the body after a long time, and bring about premature death in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"And if the skin is thick, then it is necessary to hurt .ij. times: the first time for subtlety in making the deep vein route."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the skin is very thick, then it is necessary to hurt the third time; and when we want to milk the blood little by little, then we should hurt only once."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	"And if we want to extract blood, then we should do it often; and if the skin is thick, then we should finish it completely, and the end should be that the vein bursts suddenly,"
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and to those who have thick leather and hard skin, that you ooze the openings of the suction cups with oil that opens and dissolves.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with seed oil of the cucumber;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in veal, with nettle oil, or with lily oil, or with chamomile oil, or other kind of oil.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if it is very cold and thick, take almond oil, or balsamite oil, or aniseed oil, and other oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one has a painful swelling and large pores, then it is not necessary to put oil on.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it should be washed after the wind has passed, whether it is warm or cold water, or water from a mulberry, or water from a cucumber, or water from porcelain, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if one has moisture, if it rises thus, or water from myrrh, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if one has large superfluities, they rise from old wine, or water from thistle, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and is not well to use a suction cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or.ij. and do not sleep after the suctions,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he be washed when he needs to be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are prone to anger, and whose blood is too hot and fiery;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he eats cold things, such as grapes, endive, lettuce, and asparagus, and milk, and similar foods;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and let there be small fish, and a cage, and wet meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and let there be small fish and birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that it rains, so as to drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some people no more wine or musk before or after the wind, in order to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle with the salt, but it only works if you are warm.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are used to hurt are those placed on the liver, and on the stomach, and the podagra, and on the belly and the buttocks and the rain and the thigh, because this member does not feel pain when it is bitten.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does not do so except to attract blood from member to member,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do with the breasts when the milk comes out; by removing the viscosity that is in the member, as we put leeches on the belly and the buttocks to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and bone the pain, when there is operation or stone, if bone by its attractive power accidently the operation, or deserts the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so do this when you put it on the liver and on the mouse when there is wind held back,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are empty prepared to suck so little; and never are they prepared together fire, and no time the water of the well,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as such as diseases of the lungs, and in this way the suction cup is filled with hot water, or water in which it has cooked herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be 3 inches long and half a palm in diameter, and it should have a small hole at the center, about the size of an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be made of brass, so that it does not burn the patient when applied to the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have a brass or iron crossbar in the middle for a handle;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and long and short ones according to the disease and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups of children are different from old people, and thin people from fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And it is necessary to put this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle of wax or .i. smoothly, and put it in the middle of the suction cup at the root of the limb which is in the middle of the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your two hands are on the hole that we have said, so that when you put it on, if there is steam, and then remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the lining as before, and renew it often, if you need to do so.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup that is used for pleurisy, there is no verge or hole, and it is only useful when it is plain of water, and is placed on the limb only a little.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	And it is not possible to apply suction cups except in limbs where there are small spaces, such as the lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the skin of the chest, if it is thin like two fingers or a nose, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using them is that when you find suction cups that are in clear fresh water, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in honey, until they are family, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then heal the wound and the abscess, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the poultices;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are healed and have grown, and where you can put a poultice, you put it on, for that is good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the leg thus, and then dip it in water, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if it is too warm after the body of the snake, then a linen towel in cold water, and put on it, as long as the snake is stiffened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many snakes, then put on it crushed vitriol or garlic and similar things, as long as they are stiffened;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the ground half of peeled peas, and let them burn at the fire, now they will be stiffened;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work to do, then take other snakes.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the blood will not take up, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you put in an needle as long as it shoots out blood.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then lay them on, and soon as they feel the pain, so they die;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are crying, then sprinkle on a little powder of aloes and marjoram, or ash, so they will cry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapter of this book is necessary many times in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of breakages and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, you who read this, that the wise men have never poured this paste, and neither have they ever read about it in any of their old books or letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange to us in our land, for I never found any good one before;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except that by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the preceding twenty chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we say in this book the sums of speech and the chapters where wisdom is placed, and delay on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble craft, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture, dislocation, twist, or strain comes to anyone, it is appropriate that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing else can save him, so as not to be weak of heart, or infirm, or old;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if his temperature is not very high or too low; and do not drink too much water, nor eat too much food, and do not fill the member with matter that causes blood loss, until you have no doubt about the apogee of fire, nor about the expansion of material in the member; but return the sick person to his usual government which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meat that grows fat quickly, or has viscosity like cooked wheat, and rice, and eggs, and pies made from dairy cheese, and poultry, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a quick healing, the nutrition must be increased, and the break must heal faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and frail will not heal or harden according to their nature by the loss of members, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but have no cure, bring together the broken ends of the bone. i. large bones that heal and join the member together as much as possible, so that it hardens as it was before; and do not stop at all from its work, and because it is necessary to feed on large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are many and various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break in the head is other than the break in the leg, or the foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the shoulder, and another in the limb, as when one cuts with a knife, like the length of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a small break at all.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each case there is an instrument, and its own special tool for restoration, according to what the memory comes back in place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the fracture of the bone is caused by what the angles are twisted and opened well from one another, and some to the presser of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or turning, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can also be that there is twisting, or a wound, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move the shoulder by hand, but put on medicines that come later, and then hold it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that goes in the shoulder, and are the .ij. parts separated, it now comes to put them equally, so that the abscesses come quickly;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if the abscesses come quickly, if you leave it for a day, as long as the abscesses are calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then put it evenly on the medicine that you can apply lightly and safely, and know that the restoration of the shoulder is easier than the restoration of those where there are pieces; then hold it, as it comes later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken in pieces, and it extends by half parts, whether it be hand or foot, or a small member of the hand, or to two strings, or to a string and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are healed, you remove by all means the additions in their places at the same time as you can, and guard against your work causing injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set the two shoulder bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well to the hand if it seems not right: if it is set well, and does not strain too much, do not press it as those who make it come from their work do with the shoulder, by chaut and contraction of the member, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are set in place, instruct the patient that he not move them, neither while watching nor sleeping, turning himself around, or by any other means.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure that the limbs are so secure that they do not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain, and it is set in place, and make sure to put it in such a position that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure that it is placed correctly, so that no awkwardness comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I know that broken members are different in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are little members, such as breast and toes and similar things: it is necessary to wrap them in linen cloth soft and subtle;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are fat, such as chest and leg: it is necessary to wrap them in a thick and sturdy linen cloth, for the thick linen cloth embraces all of the large member, and holds it steady from all sides evenly, so that there is no itchiness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then he will bend the leg a little, .iij. times or iiij. times according to the limb, and with his hand will grasp the whole length, then he will go up over the break and will hold it less tightly, so that the break then moves a little away from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and he will soften the ligament a little and a little, until you press on a great part of the healthy place, then take .i. other limb, and turn back very much over the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part of the break, and hold it gently, not too strongly or too lightly, as we said in the first line above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the leg-strings of linen or drapes, until they are all even, then lay it down completely .i. bend, and then put your well-made braces on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or abscess, put something soothing on it, and let the abscess drain, and leave it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then extract it from your bones, and make a half-inch cut for bleeding, or use a saw made of wood, or palm leaves, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the bone which one puts on the fracture is a little thicker and wider than the other bones;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also according to the size of the member, small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then tie it to the stakes also as you did at first, then tie it above on a string, like in the first place on the splinter.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	Then tighten it again, less tight than before; and it is necessary that the string be thin, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the string is thick, like those I have seen for the works of fools who make shoulder strings from linen threads, and that is a great mistake, because the shoulder cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should be less than two inches between each stake;
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pricked by the hooks of the stakes after the string has been tight, then put wool or linen rags there so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the rupture, and the cure is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not correspond to extract all the members of the first day when they are broken.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it does not correspond to put splints before 2 or 3 days or according to the injury of the abscess; but
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the manner of the ancient splints to restore the rupture, dislocation and torsion: and it is that you take the flour that holds on the walls of the mill, and mix it with ample egg, and put this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the splint restoring the rupture in many dispositions, especially in women and small children, for it is not too much chopped or twisted.

Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Another way of plastering for joints and bones out of place, and to soothe pain suddenly, and to fit the bone: take a new one, and moisten it with warm water and oil, and put it on the affected area. This plaster does not restore properly, but it is good for soothing hot pain in an abscess, and for properly fitting the bone.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plastering that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth-olive leaves, and grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Other way to embowel in the restoration of bone fracture and to soften the remaining of an abscess. Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Another way to embowl more strongly than the first, when an abscess lasts until the restoration of the member. Take roots of marshmallow, flax seed, borage, melilot, and windflower, and chamomile, from each one part; grind it, and mix with water from salt, or with sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that one should not put on the broken member for restoration more than a wax and oil cerot, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen states that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as mirr and aloe, and incense and similar things, such as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Other methods of plastering that are useful for lesions and pain: grind up the bones of small animals, or the feathers, and the veins, and tie them together evenly, then crush them, and make a plaster out of them, and lay it on the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then take off the plaster bit by bit, and see if the patient feels any pain, or if the bone moves out of place; if not, take off the plaster with your hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the spot, or itching, or there is no rest or swelling; then quickly take off the plaster, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea water, and dip it in the water, and lift it up, until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and lay it on a nut, until you are sure of the warmth;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and rest the inflammation of the member, and be bone the pain, then recommence the place gently, and a little plaster, and do not strain it so hard as before; and gently until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess and redness and pain and swelling are all gone, and you need to use plaster and binding, then start again, as you did at first, with equal length.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if there is no improvement in the member as we have said, do not remove the plaster until after three days or four or five or six; and never leave it on for more than twenty days; according to what you see, as long as the break-out comes closer to the shoulder joint.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then keep it on longer than before, and let it thicken its flesh as I said above; and if you see that the moisture disappears faster than it should, know that there will be no improvement. Then remove it after three days or four or five or six; and never leave it on for more than twenty days; according to what you see, as long as the break-out comes closer to the shoulder joint.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Let there be a warm water bath, every day, and this is for each part, and let there be salt in the water.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	For in this work, let there be a hot water bath, and this is for each day, and add salt to the water; and let there be a careful examination of what is wrong with the limb, so that it is restored wrongly: it is evil, and if it is painful, and I see no other remedy than to ease and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking, and there are different shapes and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For he has fractures that are made by the impact of an spear, and the collarbone breaks all the bone until syfac which is dislocated the bone, so as to do what one does or was; and for this reason this method of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear breaks the bone from above without piercing it, and is called in this language a "brisure absolue"; and the wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact from within, or a fracture, or a collarbone of stone, or a fall onto stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture, which approaches but does not touch the tendon which is outside the bone, or which is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has healed in the bone as fine as a hair, and it is a small split, so it is called this break "capillaries";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by a stone or by falling or by some other thing, and it enters the bone as a piece of wood enters a cauldron when they pour it into the cauldron; if it goes into the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in the lower part of the body, where the bones are softer, as in the case of a child's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And all these types of fractures, small pieces break like plates of metal, and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and the investigation at tents, and the carriage corrupt that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is caused by what happens when the bone is uncovered and rubbed up against, so that it opens up a black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be careful as to what happens to the patient, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of feeling, extension, clumsiness, fever, or hot sweat, and red or wrinkled skin, and other similar symptoms in multiple body parts, it is doubtful that they can be healed.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any likely accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the baby is born first to you, and it's in the winter, then it's necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month for you to do.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in the spring, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day of the month so that the tissue around the bone doesn't rot, and the accident that we have spoken of comes about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break in the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the skull, then you must split the split part thus: and it is that you press on the chief of the sick person, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the departure of blood comes with the uncovering of the bone, or abscess, then you must aid him who is in that need, and it is that you fill the place with damped linen wetted with oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calm, and be sure of the loss of blood; then begin to cut into the bone, and it is done according to .ij. ways of operation: one way is that you chop at the narrow end in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another cut wider than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you make a number of different cuts, some wide and some narrow, pointed, and made of iron; and do it lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, so that you pierce it inside, as well as you bring taillemens with tethers, not perfectly so that they pass beyond the bone, and should have above the point a margin or .i. circle, so that it does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have more, so that each comes in its place from the edge of the bone, so that you have tethers for all test; and this is the form of the .iij. ways of tethers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Here is the translation of the text:
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, if it seems to you that you rest the sharpness which is kept by the bone from all .i. other instrument resembling an incision, but it is necessary that it be more soft and more fine than the other incision;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it does not keep anything from the small bones, nor scales, if the bone is lightly tied to any instrument; then heal the wound with tenses and oils that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to work if it is that of Galen who says, which is more effective; and press it very hard, and this is his word:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you should uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture has opened up, so that when you have uncovered this part, you shall place the end of this lenticular chisel upon it, from which comes this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the section is wet in two. 2. sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then take a small mallet on top, so that you knock lightly on the bone all around, and be well aware of the tendon that is attached to it;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is fixed to the bone, so knock lightly on the bone, because when the bone is well fixed, there is no pain, and there is no fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce the skin, and cut the bone only slightly from above, and there are small pieces, then cover this roughness with a fine razor that you must have in various quantities, to apply according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are facing great razors, and after smaller ones, do not cease to do this as long as it is necessary.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and delicate shaves, you must adapt according to their shape; and this is a thing that has not yet been answered by those who have put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is infected, you must take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and dip it in oil, and put it on the wound; and you must put a poultice on top of it.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another doubled cloth, or two or three, and dip it in wine and oil, and put it on the first cloth; and make it lighter than you can, so that you do not harm the wound, then apply it above the other linen, and do not strip it off except to moisten the wound only;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it so .i. jor or 13., until the abscesses are calm, then take off, and administer drugs like roots of licorice, and flour of times, and powder of incense, and aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put on the wound, and administer sometimes drugs that do not cause itching;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and guard that the wound be clean, so you do not leave it alone or allow it to gather bowels, for when bowels gather over the brain's membrane, if they corrode and burn, they bring great harm to the patient; because when one puts a mordant drug on, if it does not dry out above it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be careful, for any bad accident may happen to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blacken does not come because of the medicine that has been put on, which has its virtue, then you must squeeze a part of honey and 2 parts of rose oil and one drape of resin, and put it on the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the cure in a way that he understands, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You know that never are broken the .ij. parts of the neck from above, or one by one for he has 12 bones; and those of the back are cartilaginous, and do not break if they are bent or twisted, but heal.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the 12 parts is broken, then you must drive your little finger or thumb from the back of the neck and set it equal to its natural position by turning it in at the index finger and out at the thumb until the neck revives according to its natural form.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain in your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if his fracture is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot return to its place, know that you put it equal to the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if his fracture is in two parts, then do not restore it another way, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or ninth day, when the abscess at the base has calmed down, then bandage it with linen cloth at the neck, if his fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bandage the other side from the first, if his fracture is there; and let the wraps be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that there is no restoration unless the tents are made wet with ash and powder of mill; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never bottle the water of the pen of an owl in place of the tents, and if it is so hot that it dries up and cracks the skin, and blows on the patient, or does whatever you see fit to do.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscesses open up while you are operating, put cotton wicks wet with rose oil or a little drop of dioxylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscesses open up, put an ointment made from wheat flour, and incense powder, infused with ash of owl, then apply it to light dressings, and do not tie the wound shut.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break is small, it is broken into small pieces, so that when it is extracted with suitable instruments, then cut off the end, and cure the things that are attached to it, and bind it together, as you do with plasters and ointments that suit it.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no pain inside the neck, then cure the wound, and put on bandages of wool, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the break in the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no pain, and the break is not very big, and it does not hurt much, except that it may be a little bit dislocated, if you can see lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	Il covient, si li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you stick your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left jaw, stick your index finger from the right hand into it, and push the break inside gently, and make the same motion with the other hand away from it, and make it equal. And if the break of the jaw has been done in .ij., it is necessary that you regulate extension by .ij. parts, as long as it remains equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth has occurred, or the rupture, if they are drawn out with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place on the broken jaw a waxed thread, and on top of it a double fabric; and place on top of that a large well-made platelet, or a piece of leather that is equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it to the muzzles that you have, and order the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the appearance has changed, if you leave it for three days, and then reset what has changed; and apply plaster to it, with flour from the mill mixed with ash or wheat flour from the husk, after you have taken off the wax; and apply a light layer of plaster, and if the plaster applies itself, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave him healthy for as long as he remains so; often he gets well in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses develop, administer as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, let no piece of the bone be osteted; if subtle, use the instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, then widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have osteted all these pieces, and if there is no delay, so that the wound is wide, and put on it plasters suitable for this, to prevent injury, as long as it is healthy.
de la forcele	Here is the first sentence of the text translated from Old French to English:
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Here is the translated text line-by-line:
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	1. The fire cautery breaks several times in front, before the shoulder, and so it is broken and dislocated in two ways: either it is broken and dislocated at one end, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore; or there is a break with an injury.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	1. And if you have to extend more, so put a round staff of cloth or other material over the shoulder of the patient, and make it large according to your need; and stretch the fire cautery, and hold the staff with your hand, so that you make equal the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder away from the opposite side, so that it comes out completely, then the patient should lie down on his back and put his ear on the ground, and let the minister lift up the shoulder blade, until the bone of the shoulder comes up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then put the break between your two sides, and if you find that it is broken, then you must split it; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then take off the instrument of the shoulder, in order to save the life of the patient:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should be like a spoon, and not a chisel, and be as wide as the bone requires and the work permits; and there are 16 chisels, if you see what I mean, and one is wide, and the others are narrow, just as the break in the bone that you made when you split the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure that the wound is hot, and if the break is small, or if you doubt about it, then employ linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come up, so moist him with oil of roses and with wine and put on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The extraction of bone, when there are wounds and bruises, is that you put on the bone with the plaster of the mill and with the ash of the oven, and put light staples on it, and put a spike through it if you need to do so.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very long band of one palm wide, then put two drapels on it, then plaster it; then take a thin stick of two fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the band, so that the top of the band is hanging;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the stake on the broken part, and turn the band over your neck, and fasten the stake on the shoulder blade; and take back each part, and when you see that the time is right, and you clearly see that the stake does not move from above the bone, then release it every day, and when it slackens, if it tightens;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and let the patient lie on his back, and bind him with a small sling from the shoulder, to raise the dislocation up; so that the dislocation of the shoulder is eased by the tightening of the sling, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not loosen it until the accident has been cured for 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and then recommence the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and hold it in place, and leave it so until it has healed; and it heals in 26 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the dislocation of the shoulder: Place the patient on their back, and bind them with a large bandage; make sure that the bandage is tight around the shoulder, and do not loosen it until the injury has healed; then apply powder from the mill with an abundance of egg white, and dust lightly, and place on a double cloth; then place on top a broad and thin board, one width wider than the shoulder, and remove the board's hair in any place where it touches the shoulder, except for the hair that is on the skin, so that the board sits evenly; and then hold it firmly in place, so that the board does not move from its position, and check it every day; and whenever it moves a little, hold it again, and make sure that the board is even if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on his back; and the shoulder will be healed after 20 days or 19.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone projects forward and there is no space to move it back, then cut into it, and make as we said in breaking up the shoulder blade to calm down an abscess, warm.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the piece
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	of the piece is never broken in the middle, but it often breaks on its own; and when it is broken in the middle, if it declines towards the side, and causes great pain to the patient, and lack of aliveness, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the vessels in the broken bone, and it smells bad.
