Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the restoration is that if the patient lies down on his back, and you put .i. cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of the .ij. ribs with your hands, and gently make it equal in all ways as much as possible so that the appearance of the bone is like; then wrap it in .i. blanket, and cover it with a thin fabric of salt, or another light thing, and lie it on the broken bone, so that it does not move; and return the ligament to its place, and tie it tightly hour by hour, and if it relaxes, release it, and remove the covering, and treat it in the manner of cures; then remove the covering, and tie it again as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I know that the rib-break does not occur except in large ribs behind the back, and at the top inside, and do not ache much unless they are thin; and the sense is good to inquiry.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And restore them so that you make the break even, if it is necessary. And then put plaster on it, and tie it with a strap, if you need to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib-break is declining inside, then the patient feels great pain and aching, as if it were weeping; for the bone rubs against the membrane; and it makes him weak, and he has a great loss of appetite, and this is a sign of bad health, and the old ones have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if one of those who serve says that it is necessary to administer meat which swells the belly, to throw the breath away.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, because when an abscess is hot, it will come if it has not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let the patient lie down.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And none of us say that we put vinegar on the head, to draw out the wind, and this is right; however, doubt I that the vinegar will attract the excesses to the head because of the weakness of the disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And said no one of them that the place of another should be covered with oil hot, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the space in front, then it is cured of the plague cure, of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that pokes through the towel, and doubt comes to the patient, then it is necessary to split on top of his place on the rib that is broken, and put there a special instrument to stop the bleeding; and then it must be sawed, and pulled lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat with poultices until he is well. And if abscesses come up, then place towels wet with rose oil on top of them; and put on his place. And cure while his place is infected, and let him rest on his rib where it hurts, until he is well.
de la brisure dou col	of the rib fracture at the throat
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No one comes to break the bones of the neck, and there is pain; and also in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when it has happened to anyone, and you see whether he will be healed or not, if you see his hands soften and swell and die, and cannot move them or stretch them out, and when you poke them with an needle, if there is no smell of it. Know that he is mortal in many states, and if they are still and smell well when they are extracted and not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the sick person is cured, if one puts cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things come to the back of the neck, and you see whether he will be healed or not, if you see his neck soften, and the accident that is in his hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without willing; and when it is sovered on its belly, if there is no excretion without willing. And when it is sovered on its back and it tries to stand up, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: if he does not work in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then that is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward if he has an abscess, put oil of rose or oil of moly on it, as long as it is calmed down; then put it on a padding of comfort and drying, and tie it with a rope, and command to the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is dislocated, then cover it with the curative poultice; and set the bone, then join the two lips of the wound together, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with poultices until it has healed; and if the bone has been broken, which is called the "bone of the knee," then take your handkerchief from your left hand, and place it flat against the other hand at your side, then apply the plaster and cover it with the cloth, if you need to; then bind it on, and if any bone has come loose, then push it back into place, and cure the wound until it is well.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the leg of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	There is a possibility that the leg hip bone may be broken, and if so, it is only a slight break at the head; and it will cause pain and swelling in the affected area, but not as much as a complete break would cause.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the setting in place is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the break; and know what the break is and what form it has; and if the break is at the head, then make it even, as long as it is in its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if it is broken long way, or she declines inwards, so make the disease go up on his belly, until the restoration of that break is arranged for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, if you put the plaster on, then put on a beam of wood or of timber, and draw out the break, so that it does not move; and fill in the space between the ribs, until the place is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the disease to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses come out, if they do not hurt, until the abscesses are even, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold them back as it should be, unless there is a bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	the dislocation of the shoulder is that which is between the collarbone and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the following two ways: in the first way you take a strong rope, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And the two shoulders are tied together with two ropes, and they are lifted up, and cut the patient on one side; then put the shoulder into a sack of rope, and then lift it over something heavy or a weight; then make the dislocated joint equal to his hands together, until the dislocated joint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	In the other way is that one should sit the patient on his back, and tie his hand to his collar, then command two ministers that one who is on the dislocated shoulder's side should hold it at its sides, and the others should stretch each of them to their parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Et s'il le poignent à leur naissance, on lui retire les yeux qu'ils ne bougent pas tant qu'ils naissent.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	Et si tu vois que l'extraction soit plus forte, si on tire.i. le lien des os la brisure, et sur la brisure, et on étend chaque ministre à sa part. Et si la brisure est proche du chef de l'épaule, il convient que tu mettes.i. le lien moien des os l'assèle, et.i. autre vers le coute, desoz la brisure; et aussi si la brisure est devers le coute, il convient mettre.i. le lien légèrement, sans travail, tant que la brisure soit égale sur le coute; puis on met égale la brisure, si comme il convient, et on la tire, si les apôtres chaus n'y viennent.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Et si tu doute que l'os ne se déplace pas, utilise des étais, et place sur la brisure une estelle plus large et plus forte que les autres, et espace chaque estelle de deux espaces, et rende chaque estelle aussi grande qu'elle dépasse la brisure de deux espaces de chaque côté; puis entraîne sur les étais, ainsi comme je l'ai dit au début du chapitre sur le chapistre sur la brisure, plus fort et moins en éloignant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the seat of the stars, and the extraction, as we said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the incisions warm, leave it tied until the seventh day, as we said; then examine each .ii. days the thread, so that itching does not spread or come to place, or the new growth cannot come to the member because it is too strained. If it is ordered, as we said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if such an accident does not come, if he does not free it until after three days or more, and the patient lies on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and sets out the shoulder with a plain cloth of even wool, and examines each hour during the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, or is not softened by the ligature; if it responds to the power of medicine, and gives him meat as we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle level; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick. It is customary for the shoulder and leg to be freed after ten months; and then he must free it and administer baths and medicines of ointments to apply to the joint. And if the stiffness is ugly and hard, let him wait to free it for one day or more.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of 2 bones, which are called the "fociles," one of which is small, and this one extends the fist; and the other is large, and it is that which extends beyond the little one on the side; perhaps the large focile breaks by itself, or the small one, and perhaps they break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small focile is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is ill, and it hurts more than when they are broken together. If only the small focile is broken, then the proper thing is to extend it lightly, and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large focile, then you should strain it more strongly; and extend it on .i. side, and turn the fist of the hand above all the other bones, and the small fingers below all the others, and make the patient cross his arms over himself, and a minister extends one arm to the dislocated part at his side, or at his hip, and another minister at the top; and then he makes him even according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then each one should be put in its place, and if any of them are loose, then you should hold them with your hand, and you cannot restore it to its place, then you must bend it and the bone. As we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the cauterization there is an ulcer, I have spoken of it to the singular chapter; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the treatment of ulcers there is an ulcer, I have spoken of it to the singular chapter; so take care.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, as itching that comes to the member, so it is necessary that you soak the member in warm water until the itching is relieved; and let the member rest without straining it. And then begin again with the cauterization, and if the lacing is soft and the bone has been dislocated, and similar things, then treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the member is too strained, so that it cannot be relaxed, then it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it thus for some days, until the tension is relieved, and then apply the cauterization.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Et s’il ne vient aucun de ces choses que nous avons dit à malade, si non le délier jusques à .XX. jours; ou enquintrant, puis li pent les mains à son cou, et soit ses cols égaux, et se garde de mouvement et de déguisement, et dort sur son dos; et saisisses que ceste briseure est rétablie en .XXX. jours ou en .XXXv., et par aventure en .XX. jours, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.
de la brisure de la main	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, unless you release him after 20 days; or when he is in a fit state, then he will hold his hands at his neck, and make his shoulders equal, and keep them from movement and deformity, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in 60 days or 65, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and on both hands there are few fractures, and only a little pain comes;
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or painful, let the patient sit straight and upright with his hands in front of him, equal; then put your hand on an extended cloth, and extend the members of the broken bones, and put them together evenly; and apply plaster and stabs, except for the knuckles, then wrap it in 1.5 yards of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks in the garden behind the plant, then make a rod of drapelz, and instruct the patient that he should pull it out at its root; and then extract it with a long drapeil, and make it straight as the plant from his hand, and extract it, as it comes.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the back, then you should put a stake in, and another above the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and sewed the ligature between the two hands.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks at one of the two hands, then you should make it even, as it comes; and extract it with the plant, and if you see that it does not move, then raise a small straight stake to lift the break, and do not move it; and if the break is at one of the other two, then make them even, and bind them together, holding them tightly, so they don’t move, or you will strain them, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken shoulder
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the hip are often broken, and we can see it clearly when it turns forward and backward; and the repair is done by bonding above and below the break.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends each minister [helper] to his side evenly; and it is when the break is made in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near the root of the hip, then one of the lines goes towards the knuckle of the hand, and the other goes behind the break; and if it is near the knee, then one line goes down the thigh, and the other up towards the break; and then he places the bone even with his two hands according to its natural form, and then he applies the plaster, and ties it up, so that the blood does not flow.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it be left to rest and then return to your work and your treatment; the time has been well spent.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the break. i.e. bandage hard double in .ij. or .iij., and wait for the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the birth, and pour. i.e. thread long between the thigh and the leg, release the knee cap, and bring the chief with the thread above; then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put on the break staves, and put a staff on the bone of the leg; then employ the place out between the leg and the thigh of drapes soft to put equal the stretching, then begin to tie in form. iij. twists or iiij. on the break; and as you go more up on the break, and less the stretch; then enter in .ij. threads that you have poured between the leg and the thigh, and lie .iij. staves that are above, then go back to the release at the chief of the thread, until you come away from the foot; and the stretching, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, then if it comes ne abortion or swelling or other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, if it releases, and addresses that which comes to it, if like we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hold, if it is necessary to take them out, if one can; and if one cannot, if it is necessary to split the place, and to draw forcibly; and cure it as we have said, until he is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is broken the thigh in this way that one sets staves, if like in the aid and where arm; however, in this restoration made does not sound the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the wound heals in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	For in the knee joint there is sometimes a little fracture, but it often heals several times. And if it fractures, let it be only a crack or a hole, and not a whole break, because otherwise it hurts a lot.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the restoration be such that what is broken on one side is made equal to it on the other, as much as possible; then put plaster, and put a round stake, if you need it, and fasten it so that it is secure, then give treatment to all injuries as we have said for other fractures, like an ape and others. Put what is right for each accident, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	That the leg has .ij. bones, of which one is called by right "mustelz" and the others are called "foscile"; and all other breaks are like those of the arm equally, and the work is done in the same way as that of the arm equally, and the dislocations are done likewise.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, so the leg turns round on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bones are broken, so the leg turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, then you feel great pain and see it clearly; and then turn back to extension. Then extend, and make it even, and tie the stars evenly; but nevertheless, it is necessary that the break be ugly, and there are many pieces, so the extension is lesser and lighter; and adjust according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, then take 13. faixes of rope that purple the leg on one side and another, and are long from the knee to the hip until the heel; then wrap them in 13. leus 1. bendeil from above and below, and tie them in the middle, and at this tying no leg shall decline towards the right or left, and so is good; and none administer 1. bers of rope long from the leg, and if it is of rope, and put on the leg to ward off movement, and properly do one on the break where there is a wound; and move each day the leg to see if there is an abscess or another accident; and heal it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone break of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no bone break, but the bones of the foot come in various breaks and positions, and there comes only one break from fire.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of your foot are broken and you see those bones overtake each other, then place this person down on the ground like they want to walk, and then now put your foot on their own, where the bones have risen up again, press it with all your strength until it comes back to its own place; then put the paste on and stamp it, and put a little plate in the navel of the foot that has 1.5 square inches of plain cloth, then hold it forward, and when you have wrapped the drapes and other things you need around them.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	After three or four days have passed, because you will find the bones even if they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there is one of the two broken, then restore it, as we have said for the hand; and put a stake according to its length on the broken side, and let it be a little wider, then put the little plate on that I spoke of next to the foot, and press it forward; and if there are 1.5 or more, or more, broken ones, then put a stake according to their quantity, wrapped in 1.5 drapes of linen, and press the plate against the navel of the foot; and may it be well under the chief of the plate the belly of the foot is.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget any other things that I have said for the others that break, when we have said it; and assist each injury in any way possible.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone with the knuckle joint
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the arm bone is fractured with the knuckle joint, if the fair lady is seated upright, then she should be inclined to the back part of the body, and supported from behind; then stuff the socket with cotton, and put in as much as a fist; then let the lady stand up, and touch her back slowly, and then take out the cotton, until it comes into the socket, and set the bone with the fist; and when she urines, if she holds the cotton, and when she has finished, replace it, and so do this. 20 days or more: thus will the fracture be healed, and the lady will be cured, take a bladder of wild boar, and tie a cord to the navel, and pour all the bladder into the socket; then blow into the cord forming a shape, until the bladder is inside: so the socket will come back to life; then stuff it with cotton, and let it be like that for some days, until it has healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the arm bone of the man or woman is fractured, if it is restored as we have said in the book on the femur; and these fractures are not hidden from those who put their study and effort into them, and hear my book. For the fracture symbolizes many things in the right way to restoration: listen to it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the vagina, when it is fractured, take a bladder of goose and pour into the vagina; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for .iij. days or more, and it will be healed in hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	of rupture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is appropriate for him who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or limb, to be healed now, so that the healings which we have said witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, unless there is a vitriol stain, then you have nothing else, then start to restore the rupture in that very hour, or that day, so that the abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses come, unless you leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the abscesses are calm and you do not touch them nor on the third nor on the fourth day, because you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if his nose is broken, it appears on the cheek, so that you put it with a light hand to your cheeks with small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not fit your hands to make them equal in length, then take this iron instrument which is 5.6 inches long, and its width is according to the amount of the wound; and for this one is skilled at the miring so that he employs 3 or 4, according to what he needs in each cure of a break; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member when you open it, and be sharp in front and thick in the middle towards the front:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", because the bent shoulder should be placed on top of the head of the bone; and it is struck once, as long as it revives, and they are equal to each other. And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot take the bone well, then you must chop off the head of the bone until the instrument can take it properly.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back together as we have said, then with an appropriate instrument, or scalpel or chisel, in your power; then remove what is left of the bone in small pieces.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the jaw is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position. If it is in its natural position, then wet it with wine-styptic black, and clean it properly; and do not place wax or anything else on the wound where there is oil, lest it cause pus and corruption to come forth; then administer poultices when you have restored the jaw, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around according to the quantity of the wound, and be well aware that the wound should not be constricted with the fracture; and many times this has been done to the sick person, or dead or corroding none of them ever; and the extractions are more soft and less sore than those of the other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that bad accidents may come forth, as we have said, and you feel pain at the site, then it is not appropriate to place poultices on; but wrap it in place of poultices with hard cloths, and bind them. And when you see after one day or two days that a bow has formed at the wound's edge, then take off what you have placed on it with vinegar, and apply healing ointments, as with four-part herbal ointment and others.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen and re-bind the member three times a day, in the morning and at dusk, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the bow can run down leichtly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if someone runs through, and he cannot hold it but returns to its place, knowing that there are little pieces of bone, so you must cut the wound with a knife, and remove all these troublesome pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula appears at the place or any other corruption, then you must cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, as the bone of the chest or shoulder, and other large limbs, do not pull it out, because many times death comes; but leave it to putrefy; perhaps later. After 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of bruses that come from the sudor
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of the broken one, most especially when it is near the joint, and this is an ugly thing to see in the form of the limb; and by chance cannot make the limbs do their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that we are fresh: if you administer stinging medicines, as aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcocollous substances, such as acacia, and others like them; or do not use any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine of the stings, or with a lot of honey or oil; and put them on the lump in piles, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for many days; and then unbind it, and start again, until the nodules are hard; or you hold it to a piece of glass carefully made; because the property of glass is that it hardens all the swellings on the limbs; and if the nodule has become hardened like stone, it needs to be opened, so that the surplus appears, or you cut it off with a razor, until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the limbs are weak and slender from a variety of causes: either because it was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or because it had too many ligatures, and could not receive the blood supply to the member; or because of a great amount of inflammation; or because of too much movement at the wrong time; or because it had little blood in its body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the torso flexible, until the number of sores increases in it; and give him baths, and provide him with pleasure and rest; then put wax on the member, so that the wax attracts his great thirst, and pour on it often with fresh water, until the thirst runs into the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the dislocated limb after the cure
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, however, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish people who say that you must break the member all over again, and many fools have done this in our land; and these treatments are blamed, and great harm comes to them, and perhaps they die; however, if the nodules and torments are fresh, it is good that they be soaked in hot water, or with soft herbs that are cooked, such as vismavine leaves, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the fetid substance made therefrom, so as to make an ointment that softens, such as the one made of myrrh well done, and you take the muscovy oil of vismavine, and confound it with lard or oil of seed-cake, and make an ointment thereof; or you take fat figs, and grind them with hay of kolin, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And no bone is kneaded by hand to rub continuously and repeatedly; and make movement of the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if it is twisted and hardened, as it often is in stones, then it must be cut with a small, light knife, and put resin and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back into place, without any delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, and the veins swell up, and by chance one sets them back to their place; for that it is not good to move them when they are swollen: many times causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when it comes, treat the disease, and then leave it, until the abscess is calm; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and heal each member as the injury heals in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the potions for dislocations of the shoulders until the joint is pierced.
des mandibules	the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Now let the jaws be dislocated from above, and the dislocations of both are according to 19 ways: or they are a little out of their places, and soften a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the loins, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocations are small, return them by means of these eight dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it quickly in the hospital, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in this manner that the ministers rub the head of the sick person, and pour a little oil from one of his hands on the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, then the dislocation is of 19 parts; and the other two hands should be apart, so that they can move it all around. And command to the sick person that he softens his jaws, and moves them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he makes the wound even, as it comes to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And bring it back with a gentle hand, especially if the two mandibles are together, so that you heat it slightly with hot water and oil, gently bringing it back; do not tarry in bringing it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they have been brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is well closed with a softener, put it on a drape wet with a paste made of oil and wax, then lightly touch it with molasses while it is still warm;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his cheeks between 15 inches (the width of the hand), so that he does not move to the left or right, nor make any effort to improve his position, but eat light food, as long as the pains are relieved, and the mandibles are no longer sore;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then if it seems light, and do not work to open the mouth for chewing and drinking, as long as the jaw is well tied and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their places in an hour, and are not returned to their places, then there come fevers and normal colds, and by chance intestinal solutions, and by chance vomiting of clear fluid only.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then you know that it is a death sentence; and many times dies he who has it, in seventeen days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from the coast down to the extension of the body, and is dislocated several times at the back, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and extends his arms; and then press the joint with your palm, and it will return; and then put on the plaster and bandage, and tighten it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the head which is on the coast cannot dislocate; if not, and if it is dislocated at all times, let him return to his place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient that he rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and also here is how to reset the shoulder when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	That the shoulder is dislocated only because of these two ways: that one is dislocated to the part of the socket; and the second is to the part of the bone; and by chance it is dislocated to the upper part, and this happens little.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the nubs; and many times dislocates out of the socket towards the assembly, however much this hurts him, because at this he will go to hospital; those who have enough money, they hurt themselves, and return hurt.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance there are some people who break or damage, and heat the shoulder with a hot apoplexy, and think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is then necessary for you to test it, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And is recognized the dislocations when it is swallowed toward the shoulder, and makes a difference between the ill and the healthy shoulder, and you will find between them a manifest difference;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and dislocates the shoulder to the chest, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to its side, nor make any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upward, it may be hidden, for you will find it clearly at the chest;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this method of dislocation is not to be used when it is new, or when the patient has become ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister takes the patient's hand up, then places the splint on the armature, and pushes the joint upwards to its place; and the minister takes the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it down; immediately there will be a great deal of movement.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said with the hands two days later, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the minister should give a softening and soothing infusion, as of alfalfa and fenugrec and melilot in water, and be given;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	and then he should lie down on his back, and place a wooden splint on the shoulder blade, not too soft nor too hard, then put the minister's heel on the splint, and pull the patient's hand up;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and other ministers wash out the head of the disease so that it does not move downward; this shoulder returns right now, and see how you will remove it according to this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and so that you make him present .i. a person who is greater than the disease; and let it be right next to the coast, and press down this shoulder from the back of the disease, and lift up the shoulder upwards so that the disease hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and other ministers pull the hand of the disease downward toward the belly. And if the disease is too light, then put something heavy on it, and let the dislocation return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And the ramie is also done in another way: and it is fixed  .i. a long piece of wood on the ground, whose length is like a pistol, and is not too thick or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then let the patient lie down, but with a sheet over him, and the patient be standing up longwise; then let his hand be extended below another one forming a bridge, and the joint will return to its place securely.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take .i. twig of an arm of great and iii. fingers wide, which has the head turning for muscled bones to enter perfectly dislocated the assele, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then let the head be placed on a sheet, so that it does not hurt the patient, then let it be dislocated the assele of the patient; and extend your arms above the head, and place the shoulder on the arm, and the hand at the head, then place the arm on a block of wood of a certain size, and let it hang by one side: the joint will now return.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way it is, then you must put a ball of wool the same size under the assele; then set the plate of powder from the mill, with incense and ambergris, on all the shoulder and around, then draw it out under the assele coming, and tie it to the plate, and embrace the hand at the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he suck a little while the members are comfortable, for he will heal sooner; and then suck after .viij. days or thereabouts, and move him; and if he is firm and is not softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved from its place due to moisture that has come or for some other reason, you must apply the cauterization to three parts, as we have described it before or with the paste of the cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you have done all this, and after .vij. days it slides away, and the joint cannot hold up the arm in its place, then you know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and you know that the joint has not returned to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is to the right of the loins, and the mammary glands, or behind, is made by an impact, and the extension of the hands, and I administer another place; and treat as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes greasiness to the limb, and late movement, then the patient uses oil many times until that greasiness is gone, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation from the joint
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Says that the joint dislocation has been displaced to the extremities, and returns to its extremities; and if it is displaced from all sides, most notably in front and behind, and the dislocation is not properly reset, for we can clearly see and feel it; and let it be displaced according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the healthy one, if you can see it openly. For the joint is deformed, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you bring it back in this way as the leg is healed, for if the leg was healed, it would be a grief to bring it back; and by chance cannot be brought back from all and everywhere, most especially when it is at the rear; so much worse than the other dislocations, and is of great pain, and perhaps comes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is thus, when it is such that you can bring it back, that you extend its hand to your 2 hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands between the thumb and the finger, from behind and from before, and put the joint back into its wrist together, or at the root of its palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, bring it back when it doubles its hand back to its hand, and lift up the root of the palm with the thumb which is behind.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, bring it back with strong extension; and there are two who extend the arm, and they hold the two ends of a long and wide cloth, so that it does not move in the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then you have enveloped a double-cloth long and wide.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when he applies his hand to the joint, if he does not rub it with any oil for ease of movement, then tighten the joint properly until it regains its position;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, if applied with dry plaster and tightened properly, and the arm is held at the shoulder of the sick person, and left for a few days, then it is released.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint has set properly in its place, then release the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not set well, then begin again with the plaster and the bandage, and leave it in this way for a few days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after resetting the joint, and it mutates, then bathe and massage it well, and press until it is relieved; or put a layer of sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then wash and dry it out;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when he sweats, he gently rubs the joint, then puts the new one on, and then goes in or bath; and so does .ij. times or .iij., until it is healthy; and if you see it, put it on the end of a wet loaf of bread that has been heated, and strain it up; and it will come back to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand is loosened, and the recovery is lighter than that of other joints However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, when it is loosed, so that the joint may be swollen or an abscess may form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the remapping is that you put the bad hand on a table, and extend its fingers, and look at it so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and squeezes it until it comes back to life.
