Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	All the same, you must make sure it is properly positioned; then place the patient's arm on a table with its hand extended and drawn back.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then place the patient's hand on the table, and examine the appearance of the joint; if it returns to its position now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then cut off a piece of flesh from the thumb, and leave it there as a reminder.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back to its position after several days, then let the joint twist.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and is of no use to the patient until his hands are wet, and cannot extract anything at all: so know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; otherwise there is another cause than that of extracting by means of a delicate fire, and possibly nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in place, put it on the plaster we have said, then extract and leave it there. v.jors, then unstick it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, if the moist heat of water, and rub until it is cured.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two hands.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	None of these are dislocated at all to either side of the hand, none to the back of the palm or to the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then are they two, and press the dislocation towards your knuckles until it comes back, then hold the head of the two together, and push it towards the part where it is connected;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and then leave it.ij. days, and then make it even again that day; and if it is tight, let it move again, and then hold it in place; and do this often, until it has become loose, so that it does not move again; and then let it rest, and let it heal; and when it is healed,
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing if it is dislocated on the palm side of the hand, and do so as you have done before until it is healthy; and do the same thing if it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Do to dislocation of the shoulder bone at the arm,
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck or shoulder is dislocated, or multiple joints are out of place, without proper treatment, it leads to death quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the excrements come out without control, they cannot be held back, and many times the limbs become weak, or the arms or legs.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the neck becomes mute at three parts; that which is mute at the back is called "gilboize".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If it is due to a childhood malady, then there is a cure; if not, there will be no cure or recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those that come from falling down, or from blows, or from similar things, the old manner of curing them with great words has not been of much benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have simplified it according to my intention, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the childhood malady that comes before, there is neither medicine nor cure;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also say that it comes straight in .ij. sides, and can not be cured but properly who comes at the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	is that the patient is laid down flat on his back in a long, even position, and has had an extraction of pus so that he does not get bruised;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put 1. log of fire in the earth at the head, and 1. log by the side, and tie a string over the patient's body at the shoulders, and 1. log between the knees, and 1. log between the feet;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and the two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the other by the side, among the 2 logs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and are firmly closed, the thread as we have said, and the mirrour puts its palms on the spine, until he revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if he does not recover with this treatment, take a large bowl of two arms long, and cut a hole in the wall, and place the patient on one side, and pour the contents of the bowl over the head, then put the middle of the bowl on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and place the mirror's tips on the other side of the bowl, and press firmly until he revives; and if you see this, do it with a ring which turns the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	and put two fire-sticks on the patient's head with a long space between them; and place one hand over each stick, and wrap a palm of space around them.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and let each stick i .e. pine, or it turns over, and are the sticks firmly in the ground so that they do not move, and between each two sticks is one stick turning, for so the bond turns, and let 1 . j . small sticks of a palm long, to turn the bond;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then the bond that is between the axles towards the top of the tree, and the other bond towards the pegs at the opposite end, and each of the ministers turns his bond on all the bonds, and the master puts the string even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on desicative plaster with a lot of incense, and then the staples, and then the stele of a tablet of 1. iij. feet long, that so he puts the length of the leg of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then the bond of a bond, as we have said, and uses the patient subtle nourishment, until he is healthy;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if anything comes at the end of health, so administer soft and soothing medicines, with the stele that we have said above; and do not give a piece of silver,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and there is never a appearance in the back of the spine of the backbone, and take care that it is not dislocations; and this is the bone which opens, so that one should not have any presumption: by chance might come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the hip joints
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	come only dislocations, and not at all as with the other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to.iiij. parties: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more inside, and less in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocations inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is further away, and opens more the legs of the sick man than those of the healthy one, and cannot double his knee on fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the limb is swollen with heat due to an abscess, because the head of the hip comes from there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that injury if it goes wrong, is that this accident is opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that injury if it goes wrong, is that his leg is well in accordance with the accomplishment; nevertheless, he does not double himself because of the pain, and if one makes him walk, he cannot walk forward, and holds back his urine, and swells his ankle, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that injury if it goes wrong, is that he cannot extend his leg, double himself, and his leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the hip is at the place where the ribs are joined.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If the patient is older and has had previous dislocations, and it takes time to happen, there will be no cure; it is only necessary that he not be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those who have had a fresh dislocation, and there are four kinds of dislocations, if you hurry to put the joint back together, turn it in and out, and move it from side to side; perhaps it will come back into place, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not come back into place in this way, take very strong assistance, and support the leg with two hands or a bandage tied to the knee joint;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and place another minister's hand above it in a way that it presses its hands together, then tie a strong bandage over the shoulder; and another minister should hold his hair;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend upward and downward altogether, so that the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains standing.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to all three appearances, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, then you must cure the patient's appearance. When the dislocation is in the garden, you must lie on your side facing downward, then bring the bandage to the root of the crotch, and the loop that is away from the anus, then extend the bandage upward toward the anus, and upward toward the thigh;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then have other ministers hold his arms, and embrace the large loop of the crotch, and extend it toward the back form: now it will return to its place; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot fasten it in this way that we have said, then you must bind the .ij. feet of the patient together with a strong cord beneath the .ij. heels, and above the .ij. knees, and so that the injured leg is longer than the other by .ij. two more.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then hang him by the neck of a mast, and set him on the ground 2 arms' length away; then command 1 minister to embrace the neck of the chest, and let others hang with the patient, who embraces the chest firmly, for now the joints will return to their place without difficulty.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation has returned to its place, so lie the patient, as we have said in that which concerns giddiness, and tie 1 cord properly upon the injured leg, and also upon the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put 2 torches at the head and another one between the feet of the patient; then set a torch between the cheeks of the patient;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and set a wet flag around, that it does not burn the patient, then each minister extends to him, and the doctor sets the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, it is good. If not, put it on .ie. a table, and press it so as we have said in the gibosity, and place the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, extend the leg that is not well far from him, and according to what I have said; and place the doctor's hand on his pain to be under the ill leg, then press with the other hand, and bring it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is in the back, extend the leg that is not well far from him, and according to what I have said; and place the doctor' hand on his pain to be under the ill leg, then press with the other hand, and bring it down towards the knee. If the dislocation is in the back, do not extend the patient far, nor raise him on the ground; rather, he should be placed as if he were lying on his side, as we have said for the bed; and place li mires sous lou malaide
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it on his face, and the line extended as we have said above, and must all press upon the joint to the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and will be done when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; so make sure the feet are fixed, and apply the plaster, and hold it with a bandage, so that the foot does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and rest for ii or iii days, then remove it, and apply the plaster; and if you see that they are even, stretch them out as before, and leave it. iij days; then remove it, and let him walk about loudly, until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation due to age
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The members are dislocated according to three ways: namely, inside and outside, behind; and not in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are these: instruct the patient that he bend his leg to his knee, and if it does not touch his knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the rehabilitation of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and if he can extend his leg, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your knees.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee at your palms, and draw back between the two, then bend the .iij. knees from the knee joint; and other ministers extend his foot, until the member returns to its place, and the signs are that he touches his knee lightly with his leg.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and place the plaster on top of it, and make the leg rest in the chest, and join them together firmly .iiij. days or iiij. days, then remove it; and do not work the patient to walk, as long as the limbs are supported.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not in place, administer stretching strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation at the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is never dislocated, and is never fully displaced inward or outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and try first on the part where it has come out.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	They bring him in if he is light, and they should gently stretch his legs to their hands when he is only slightly injured.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it has come out completely, if it is necessary that you make the patient lie down flat, and you tie him up tightly by the legs, over the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then train your feet to your hands, and then to your opposite hand. Then stretch him out, and stretch his legs well;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this 19 times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, then begin again the work, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, then make the patient sit on his back on the ground, and put a stake firmly into the ground between his buttocks, and tie the sheets around it, so that he does not hurt the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then place the minister's hand on his hip, and another minister extend the foot to his hands or to 1.a. chain, so that he holds it by the collar of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each minister equally, and the stake be next to the hip of the patient to hold it in place while it is being extended;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And then make the dislocated arm equal with his hands, and some other ministers dip the healthy leg in the dung, and the dislocation will come back slowly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is ready, so put the plaster on and press down, and form the strain, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard against the tendons behind the ankle, so that the bonds are not too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then let it be .ij. days or .iij., and if the strain has loosened, then let it be left for one more day, and if it is still loose, go to see the patient every three days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term, it is not yet safe that he does not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come out, so it is necessary that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are well.
des dois	the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if it is properly extended without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in the hip or leg, so it is necessary that you place the patient on their back or on a table all straight, and put your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot in this form, until he comes back;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is even, and there is nothing open, so set the foot of the leg on a table at 1.2 degrees, then remove it while forming, and leave it 1.2 days, then let it be; and let it rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When the wound comes with the dislocation, and it is reset, many times the patient has died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you have not used it long, and if you are not compassionate and patient and slow to anger, do not be arrogant:
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things soothing an abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if I restore now the member to its place, so that the abscesses may come;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is in place, then administer soothing ointment to the abscess, and cure the wound, if necessary, with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a fracture with broken bones, and the joints are displaced, do as we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and you keep from entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will cost you much according to your Creator, and for the sake of your arms and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	And let not the fire cautery
